A : The first letter of the English and of many other alphabets. The capital A of the alphabets of Middle and Western Europe, as also the small letter (a), besides the forms in Italic, black letter, etc., are all descended from the old Latin A, which was borrowed from the Greek Alpha, of the same form; and this was made from the first letter (/) of the Phoenician alphabet, the equivalent of the Hebrew Aleph, and itself from the Egyptian origin. The Aleph was a consonant letter, with a guttural breath sound that was not an element of Greek articulation; and the Greeks took it to represent their vowel Alpha with the a sound, the Phoenician alphabet having no vowel symbols.

The best is the heartwood of Caesalpinia echinata, a leguminous tree; but other trees also yield it. An inferior sort comes from Jamaica, the timber of C. Braziliensis and C. crista. This is often distinguished as Braziletto , but the better kind is also frequently so named.

By : Out of the common path; aside; -- used in composition, giving the meaning of something aside, secondary, or incidental, or collateral matter, a thing private or avoiding notice; as, by-line, by-place, by-play, by-street. It was formerly more freely used in composition than it is now; as, by-business, by-concernment, by-design, by-interest, etc.
By-law : A local or subordinate law; a private law or regulation made by a corporation for its own government.
Byss : See Byssus, n., 1.

Cabal : Tradition; occult doctrine. See Cabala
Cabaret : a type of restaurant where liquor and dinner is served, and entertainment is provided, as by musicians, dancers, or comedians, and providing space for dancing by the patrons; -- similar to a nightclub. The term cabaret is often used in the names of such an establishment.
Cabin : A small room; an inclosed place.
Cabbiri : Certain deities originally worshiped with mystical rites by the Pelasgians in Lemnos and Samothrace and afterwards throughout Greece; -- also called sons of Hephaestus (or Vulcan), as being masters of the art of working metals.
Cabob : A small piece of mutton or other meat roasted on a skewer; -- so called in Turkey and Persia.
Cachalot : The sperm whale (Physeter macrocephalus). It has in the top of its head a large cavity, containing an oily fluid, which, after death, concretes into a whitish crystalline substance called spermaceti. See Sperm whale.
Cackle : To make a sharp, broken noise or cry, as a hen or goose does.
Cacogastric : Troubled with bad digestion.
Cactaceous : Belonging to, or like, the family of plants of which the prickly pear is a common example.
Caddow : A jackdaw.
Cadenza : A parenthetic flourish or flight of ornament in the course of a piece, commonly just before the final cadence.
Caddie : A Scotch errand boy, porter, or messenger.
Caecal : Of or pertaining to the caecum, or blind gut.
Caesural : Of or pertaining to a caesura.
Cage : The drum on which the rope is wound in a hoisting whim.
Cairn : A rounded or conical heap of stones erected by early inhabitants of the British Isles, apparently as a sepulchral monument.
Cajoler : A flatterer; a wheedler.
Calabash : A water dipper, bottle, bascket, or other utensil, made from the dry shell of a calabash or gourd.
Calamitous : Producing, or attended with distress and misery; making wretched; wretched; unhappy.
Calcar : A hollow tube or spur at the base of a petal or corolla.
Calceiform : Shaped like a slipper, as one petal of the lady's-slipper; calceolate.
Calciminer : One who calcimines.
Calcographic : Alt. of Calcographical
Calculating : Given to contrivance or forethought; forecasting; scheming; as, a cool calculating disposition.
Caledonite : A hydrous sulphate of copper and lead, found in some parts of Caledonia or Scotland.
Calendar : To enter or write in a calendar; to register.
Calf : The young of the cow, or of the Bovine family of quadrupeds. Also, the young of some other mammals, as of the elephant, rhinoceros, hippopotamus, and whale.
Calicoback : The calico bass.
Calipers : An instrument, usually resembling a pair of dividers or compasses with curved legs, for measuring the diameter or thickness of bodies, as of work shaped in a lathe or planer, timber, masts, shot, etc.; or the bore of firearms, tubes, etc.; -- called also caliper compasses, or caliber compasses.
Calker : A calk on a shoe. See Calk, n., 1.
Call : An invitation to take charge of or serve a church as its pastor.
Callidity : Acuteness of discernment; cunningness; shrewdness.
Callipers : See Calipers.
Calm : Freedom from motion, agitation, or disturbance; a cessation or absence of that which causes motion or disturbance, as of winds or waves; tranquility; stillness; quiet; serenity.
Calorifere : An apparatus for conveying and distributing heat, especially by means of hot water circulating in tubes.
Caltrap : An instrument with four iron points, so disposed that, any three of them being on the ground, the other projects upward. They are scattered on the ground where an enemy's cavalry are to pass, to impede their progress by endangering the horses' feet.
Calve : To bring forth a calf.
Calycinal : Alt. of Calycine
Cam : A projecting part of a wheel or other moving piece so shaped as to give alternate or variable motion to another piece against which it acts.
Cambist : A banker; a money changer or broker; one who deals in bills of exchange, or who is skilled in the science of exchange.
Camel : A water-tight structure (as a large box or boxes) used to assist a vessel in passing over a shoal or bar or in navigating shallow water. By admitting water, the camel or camels may be sunk and attached beneath or at the sides of a vessel, and when the water is pumped out the vessel is lifted.
Camerate : To build in the form of a vault; to arch over.
Camous : Alt. of Camoys
Campaign : The period during which a blast furnace is continuously in operation.
Campeachy : Logwood.
Camping : Lodging in a camp.
Canaanite : A zealot.
Canary : Of a pale yellowish color; as, Canary stone.
Cancel : An inclosure; a boundary; a limit.
Cancerated : of Cancerate
Candid : White.
Candleberry : A shrub (the Myrica cerifera, or wax-bearing myrtle), common in North America, the little nuts of which are covered with a greenish white wax, which was formerly, used for hardening candles; -- also called bayberry tree, bayberry, or candleberry.
Candy : To have sugar crystals form in or on; as, fruits preserved in sugar candy after a time.
Cannicula : The Dog Star; Sirius.
Canker : To infect or pollute; to corrupt.
Cannabis : A genus of a single species belonging to the order Uricaceae; hemp.
Cannonade : To attack with heavy artillery; to batter with cannon shot.
Canoe : A boat made of bark or skins, used by savages.
Canon : That part of a bit which is put in a horse's mouth.
Canonship : Of or pertaining to Canopus in Egypt; as, the Canopic vases, used in embalming.
Canting : of Cant
Cantalever : A bracket to support a balcony, a cornice, or the like.
Canter : To move in a canter.
Canticoy : A social gathering; usually, one for dancing.
Canton : A small community or clan.
Cantred : Alt. of Cantref
Canvass : To search thoroughly; to engage in solicitation by traversing a district; as, to canvass for subscriptions or for votes; to canvass for a book, a publisher, or in behalf of a charity; -- commonly followed by for.
Cap : Anything resembling a cap in form, position, or use
Capable : Possessing adequate power; qualified; able; fully competent; as, a capable instructor; a capable judge; a mind capable of nice investigations.
Capapie : From head to foot; at all points.
Capellane : The curate of a chapel; a chaplain.
Capias : A writ or process commanding the officer to take the body of the person named in it, that is, to arrest him; -- also called writ of capias.
Capital : Having reference to, or involving, the forfeiture of the head or life; affecting life; punishable with death; as, capital trials; capital punishment.
Capitally : In a capital manner; excellently.
Capitular : Of or pertaining to a chapter; capitulary.
Capitulum : A knoblike protuberance of any part, esp. at the end of a bone or cartilage. [See Illust. of Artiodactyla.]
Capot : To win all the tricks from, in playing at piquet.
Caprice : See Capriccio.
Capsheaf : The top sheaf of a stack of grain: (fig.) the crowning or finishing part of a thing.
Capsule : A metallic seal or cover for closing a bottle.
Caption : That part of a legal instrument, as a commission, indictment, etc., which shows where, when, and by what authority, it was taken, found, or executed.
Captive : To take prisoner; to capture.
Capita : of Caput
Caracara : A south American bird of several species and genera, resembling both the eagles and the vultures. The caracaras act as scavengers, and are also called carrion buzzards.
Carat : The weight by which precious stones and pearls are weighed.
Carbazotate : A salt of carbazotic or picric acid; a picrate.
Carbonadoes : of Carbonado
Carboxide : A compound of carbon and oxygen, as carbonyl, with some element or radical; as, potassium carboxide.
Carburization : The act, process, or result of carburizing.
Carcinosys : The affection of the system with cancer.
Carder : One who, or that which cards wool flax, etc.
Carding : A roll of wool or other fiber as it comes from the carding machine.
Care : To be anxious or solicitous; to be concerned; to have regard or interest; -- sometimes followed by an objective of measure.
Careless : Having no care; not taking ordinary or proper care; negligent; unconcerned; heedless; inattentive; unmindful; regardless.
Cargoose : A species of grebe (Podiceps crisratus); the crested grebe.
Carina : That part of a papilionaceous flower, consisting of two petals, commonly united, which incloses the organs of fructification
Carl : A kind of food. See citation, below.
Carminative : Expelling wind from the body; warming; antispasmodic.
Carnal-mindedness : Grossness of mind.
Carnivoracity : Greediness of appetite for flesh.

Carryk : A carack.
Cartes : of Carte de visite
Cartilaginification : The act or process of forming cartilage.
Cartouch : A cantalever, console, corbel, or modillion, which has the form of a scroll of paper
Carus : Coma with complete insensibility; deep lethargy.
Carver : One who carves or divides meat at table.
Cascabel : The projection in rear of the breech of a cannon, usually a knob or breeching loop connected with the gun by a neck. In old writers it included all in rear of the base ring. [See Illust. of Cannon.]
Case : The matters of fact or conditions involved in a suit, as distinguished from the questions of law; a suit or action at law; a cause.
Caseous : Of, pertaining to, or resembling, cheese; having the qualities of cheese; cheesy.
Cashierer : One who rejects, discards, or dismisses; as, a cashierer of monarchs.
Casket : A kind of burial case.
Cassican : An American bird of the genus Cassicus, allied to the starlings and orioles, remarkable for its skillfully constructed and suspended nest; the crested oriole. The name is also sometimes given to the piping crow, an Australian bird.
Cassumuniar : A pungent, bitter, aromatic, gingerlike root, obtained from the East Indies.
Cast : To fix, distribute, or allot, as the parts of a play among actors; also to assign (an actor) for a part.
Cast : The assignment of parts in a play to the actors.
Castellated : Furnished with turrets and battlements, like a castle; built in the style of a castle.
Casting : The act or process of making casts or impressions, or of shaping metal or plaster in a mold; the act or the process of pouring molten metal into a mold.
Castlet : A small castle.
Castrating : of Castrate
Casuarina : A genus of leafless trees or shrubs, with drooping branchlets of a rushlike appearance, mostly natives of Australia. Some of them are large, producing hard and heavy timber of excellent quality, called beefwood from its color.
Catabiotic : See under Force.
Catafalco : See Catafalque.
Catalpa : A genus of American and East Indian trees, of which the best know species are the Catalpa bignonioides, a large, ornamental North American tree, with spotted white flowers and long cylindrical pods, and the C. speciosa, of the Mississipi valley; -- called also Indian bean.
Cataphonics : That branch of acoustics which treats of reflected sounds; catacoustics.
Catastasis : That part of a speech, usually the exordium, in which the orator sets forth the subject matter to be discussed.
Catch : To take captive, as in a snare or net, or on a hook; as, to catch a bird or fish.
Catch : A humorous canon or round, so contrived that the singers catch up each other's words.
Catchword : Among theatrical performers, the last word of the preceding speaker, which reminds one that he is to speak next; cue.
Catechistic : Alt. of Catechistical
Catelectrode : The negative electrode or pole of a voltaic battery.
Cater : To cut diagonally.
Catharine : See catherine wheel.
Catherine : Same as Rose window and Wheel window. Called also Catherine-wheel window.
Catholicism : The state or quality of being catholic or universal; catholicity.
Catlinite : A red clay from the Upper Missouri region, used by the Indians for their pipes.
Catsos : of Catso
Caucus : To hold, or meet in, a caucus or caucuses.
Cauk : Alt. of Cauker

Caustic : A caustic curve or caustic surface.
Caution : A careful attention to the probable effects of an act, in order that failure or harm may be avoided; prudence in regard to danger; provident care; wariness.
Cavalier : One of the court party in the time of king Charles I. as contrasted with a Roundhead or an adherent of Parliament.
Cave : To fall in or down; as, the sand bank caved. Hence (Slang), to retreat from a position; to give way; to yield in a disputed matter.
Cavicornia : A group of ruminants whose horns are hollow, and planted on a bony process of the front, as the ox.
Cavo-relievo : Cavo-rilievo.
Cayuse : An Indian pony.
Cede : To yield or surrender; to give up; to resign; as, to cede a fortress, a province, or country, to another nation, by treaty.
Celature : That which is engraved.
Celestial : An inhabitant of heaven.
Cell : Same as Cella.
Cellule : A small cell.
Cement : The powder used in cementation. See Cementation, n., 2.
Cenatory : Of or pertaining to dinner or supper.
Censorial : Belonging to a censor, or to the correction of public morals.
Cent : A hundred; as, ten per cent, the proportion of ten parts in a hundred.
Centennial : Lasting or aged a hundred years.
Centre : To collect to a point; to concentrate.
Centigrade : Consisting of a hundred degrees; graduated into a hundred divisions or equal parts.
Central : Alt. of Centrale

Centumviri : of Centumvir
Cepevorous : Feeding upon onions.
Cephalon : The head.
Cerago : Beebread.
Ceratospongiae : An order of sponges in which the skeleton consists of horny fibers. It includes all the commercial sponges.
Cerealia : Public festivals in honor of Ceres.
Cerebripetal : Applied to those nerve fibers which go from the spinal cord to the brain and so transfer sensations (centripetal impressions) from the exterior inwards.
Ceremonialness : Quality of being ceremonial.
Ceriph : One of the fine lines of a letter, esp. one of the fine cross strokes at the top and bottom of letters.
Ceroplastic : Modeled in wax; as, a ceroplastic figure.
Certainly : Without doubt or question; unquestionably.
Certiorari : A writ issuing out of chancery, or a superior court, to call up the records of a inferior court, or remove a cause there depending, in order that the party may have more sure and speedy justice, or that errors and irregularities may be corrected. It is obtained upon complaint of a party that he has not received justice, or can not have an impartial trial in the inferior court.
Cervices : of Cervix
Cesser : a neglect of a tenant to perform services, or make payment, for two years.
Cestraciont : A shark of the genus Cestracion, and of related genera. The posterior teeth form a pavement of bony plates for crushing shellfish. Most of the species are extinct. The Port Jackson shark and a similar one found in California are living examples.
Cetology : The description or natural history of cetaceous animals.
Chacma : A large species of African baboon (Cynocephalus porcarius); -- called also ursine baboon. [See Illust. of Baboon.]
Chafe : To have a feeling of vexation; to be vexed; to fret; to be irritated.
Chaffer : One who chaffs.
Chagrin : Vexation; mortification.
Chainlet : A small chain.
Chaise : A two-wheeled carriage for two persons, with a calash top, and the body hung on leather straps, or thorough-braces. It is usually drawn by one horse.
Chalcographist : An engraver on copper or brass; hence, an engraver of copper plates for printing upon paper.
Chalk : Finely prepared chalk, used as a drawing implement; also, by extension, a compound, as of clay and black lead, or the like, used in the same manner. See Crayon.
Challenge : To call, invite, or summon to answer for an offense by personal combat.
Chamade : A signal made for a parley by beat of a drum.
Chamberer : A civilian; a carpetmonger.
Chamfret : A chamfer.
Champignon : An edible species of mushroom (Agaricus campestris).
Chance : Happening by chance; casual.
Chandler : A dealer in other commodities, which are indicated by a word prefixed; as, ship chandler, corn chandler.
Change : A place where merchants and others meet to transact business; a building appropriated for mercantile transactions.
Channel : The deeper part of a river, harbor, strait, etc., where the main current flows, or which affords the best and safest passage for vessels.
Chant : To sing or recite after the manner of a chant, or to a tune called a chant.
Chaomancy : Divination by means of appearances in the air.
Chaparral : A thicket of low evergreen oaks.
Chapel : To cause (a ship taken aback in a light breeze) so to turn or make a circuit as to recover, without bracing the yards, the same tack on which she had been sailing.
Chaplaincy : The office, position, or station of a chaplain.
Chapter : A community of canons or canonesses.
Charred : of Char
Character : To distinguish by particular marks or traits; to describe; to characterize.
Charbon : A very contagious and fatal disease of sheep, horses, and cattle. See Maligmant pustule.
Charge : To bear down upon; to rush upon; to attack.
Charge : A bearing. See Bearing, n., 8.
Charily : In a chary manner; carefully; cautiously; frugally.
Charity : Love; universal benevolence; good will.
Charm : That which exerts an irresistible power to please and attract; that which fascinates; any alluring quality.
Charneco : Alt. of Charnico
Charter : A written evidence in due form of things done or granted, contracts made, etc., between man and man; a deed, or conveyance.
Chartography : Same as Cartographer, Cartographic, Cartography, etc.
Chase : An open hunting ground to which game resorts, and which is private properly, thus differing from a forest, which is not private property, and from a park, which is inclosed. Sometimes written chace.
Chasselas : A white grape, esteemed for the table.
Chastised : of Chastise
Chateau : A castle or a fortress in France.
Chatterer : A prater; an idle talker.
Chaussure : A foot covering of any kind.
Cheapen : To beat down the price of; to lessen the value of; to depreciate.
Cheater : An escheator.
Check : To make a stop; to pause; -- with at.
Checkered : Diversified or variegated in a marked manner, as in appearance, character, circumstances, etc.
Cheek : The side of the face below the eye.
Cheer : To cause to rejoice; to gladden; to make cheerful; -- often with up.
Cheese : The flat, circular, mucilaginous fruit of the dwarf mallow (Malva rotundifolia).
Cheiropterous : Belonging to the Cheiroptera, or Bat family.
Chelonia : An order of reptiles, including the tortoises and turtles, peculiar in having a part of the vertebrae, ribs, and sternum united with the dermal plates so as to form a firm shell. The jaws are covered by a horny beak. See Reptilia; also, Illust. in Appendix.
Chemistry : A treatise on chemistry.
Cherish : To hold dear; to embrace with interest; to indulge; to encourage; to foster; to promote; as, to cherish religious principle.
Cherub : A symbolical winged figure of unknown form used in connection with the mercy seat of the Jewish Ark and Temple.
Chessel : The wooden mold in which cheese is pressed.
Chest : A rheumatic affection of the muscles of the breast and fore legs of a horse, affecting motion and respiration.
Chevelure : A hairlike envelope.
Chevronwise : In the manner of a chevron; as, the field may be divided chevronwise.
Chiasmus : An inversion of the order of words or phrases, when repeated or subsequently referred to in a sentence
Chick : To sprout, as seed in the ground; to vegetate.
Chide : Fig.: To be noisy about; to chafe against.
Chiefless : Without a chief or leader.
Chikara : The Indian four-horned antelope (Tetraceros quadricornis).
Childhood : The state of being a child; the time in which persons are children; the condition or time from infancy to puberty.
Chilian : A native or citizen of Chili.
Chill : To check enthusiasm or warmth of feeling of; to depress; to discourage.
Chiltern : A tract of crown land in Buckinghamshire and Oxfordshire, England, to which is attached the nominal office of steward. As members of Parliament cannot resign, when they wish to go out they accept this stewardship, which legally vacates their seats.
Chimera : A monster represented as vomiting flames, and as having the head of a lion, the body of a goat, and the tail of a dragon.
Chinamen : of Chinaman
Chine : Too chamfer the ends of a stave and form the chine..
Chinone : See Quinone.
Chip : Anything dried up, withered, or without flavor; -- used contemptuously.

Chirrup : To quicken or animate by chirping; to cherup.
Chit : An excrescence on the body, as a wart.
Chivalrously : In a chivalrous manner; gallantly; magnanimously.
Chloralism : A morbid condition of the system resulting from excessive use of chloral.
Chlorite : The name of a group of minerals, usually of a green color and micaceous to granular in structure. They are hydrous silicates of alumina, iron, and magnesia.
Chloroplatinic : See Platinichloric.
Chockablock : Hoisted as high as the tackle will admit; brought close together, as the two blocks of a tackle in hoisting.
Choir : A band or organized company of singers, especially in church service.
Choke : A kind of pear that has a rough, astringent taste, and is swallowed with difficulty, or which contracts the mucous membrane of the mouth.
Choleraic : Relating to, or resulting from, or resembling, cholera.
Chomp : To chew loudly and greedily; to champ.
Chondropterygian : One of the Chondropterygii.

Choral : A hymn tune; a simple sacred tune, sung in unison by the congregation; as, the Lutheran chorals.

Choric : Of or pertaining to a chorus.

Chrism : Olive oil mixed with balm and spices, consecrated by the bishop on Maundy Thursday, and used in the administration of baptism, confirmation, ordination, etc.

Chub-faced : Having a plump, short face.

Churchwardenship : The office of a churchwarden.
Churning : The act of one who churns.
Chylous : Consisting of, or similar to, chyle.
Cicada : Any species of the genus Cicada. They are large hemipterous insects, with nearly transparent wings. The male makes a shrill sound by peculiar organs in the under side of the abdomen, consisting of a pair of stretched membranes, acted upon by powerful muscles. A noted American species (C. septendecim) is called the seventeen year locust. Another common species is the dogday cicada.
Ciceronian : Resembling Cicero in style or action; eloquent.
Cigar : A small roll of tobacco, used for smoking.
Cillosis : A spasmodic trembling of the upper eyelid.
Cinchona : A genus of trees growing naturally on the Andes in Peru and adjacent countries, but now cultivated in the East Indies, producing a medicinal bark of great value.
Cinematical : See Kinematic.
Cinnamene : Styrene (which was formerly called cinnamene because obtained from cinnamic acid). See Styrene.
Cipher : A character in general, as a figure or letter.
Circean : Having the characteristics of Circe, daughter of Sol and Perseis, a mythological enchantress, who first charmed her victims and then changed them to the forms of beasts; pleasing, but noxious; as, a Circean draught.
Circling : of Circle
Circuiteer : A circuiter.
Circulate : To cause to pass from place to place, or from person to person; to spread; as, to circulate a report; to circulate bills of credit.
Circumambulate : To walk round about.
Circumesophagal : Surrounding the esophagus; -- in Zool. said of the nerve commissures and ganglia of arthropods and mollusks.
Circumflexing : of Circumflex
Circumincession : The reciprocal existence in each other of the three persons of the Trinity.
Circumrotary : Alt. of Circumrotatory
Circumspection : Attention to all the facts and circumstances of a case; caution; watchfulness.
Circumstantially : In every circumstance or particular; minutely.
Circumvolant : Flying around.
Cirrhotic : Pertaining to, caused by, or affected with, cirrhosis; as, cirrhotic degeneration; a cirrhotic liver.
Cirrus : A soft tactile appendage of the mantle of many Mollusca, and of the parapodia of Annelida. Those near the head of annelids are Tentacular cirri; those of the last segment are caudal cirri.
Cistercian : Of or pertaining to the Cistercians.
Cite : To refer to or specify, as for support, proof, illustration, or confirmation.
Citizen : Having the condition or qualities of a citizen, or of citizens; as, a citizen soldiery.
City : The collective body of citizens, or inhabitants of a city.
Civillty : The state of society in which the relations and duties of a citizen are recognized and obeyed; a state of civilization.
Clacked : of Clack
Claim : To proclaim.
Clam : A kind of vise, usually of wood.
Clamminess : State of being clammy or viscous.
Clamped : of Clamp
Clangorous : Making a clangor; having a ringing, metallic sound.
Clap : To strike the hands together in applause.
Clapperclaw : To fight and scratch.
Clarifier : A vessel in which the process of clarification is conducted; as, the clarifier in sugar works.
Clary : To make a loud or shrill noise.
Claspered : Furnished with tendrils.
Classicalist : One who adheres to what he thinks the classical canons of art.
Classman : A candidate for graduation in arts who is placed in an honor class, as opposed to a passman, who is not classified.
Clause : A separate portion of a written paper, paragraph, or sentence; an article, stipulation, or proviso, in a legal document.
Clavicorn : One of the Clavicornes.
Claw : To pull, tear, or scratch with, or as with, claws or nails.
Claytonia : An American genus of perennial herbs with delicate blossoms; -- sometimes called spring beauty.
Cleaning : The afterbirth of cows, ewes, etc.
Clear : Able to perceive clearly; keen; acute; penetrating; discriminating; as, a clear intellect; a clear head.
Clear : To leap or pass by, or over, without touching or failure; as, to clear a hedge; to clear a reef.
Clearing : The gross amount of the balances adjusted in the clearing house.
Cleavage : Division into laminae, like slate, with the lamination not necessarily parallel to the plane of deposition; -- usually produced by pressure.
Cleavers : A species of Galium (G. Aparine), having a fruit set with hooked bristles, which adhere to whatever they come in contact with; -- called also, goose grass, catchweed, etc.
Clematis : A genus of flowering plants, of many species, mostly climbers, having feathery styles, which greatly enlarge in the fruit; -- called also virgin's bower.
Clergy : The body of men set apart, by due ordination, to the service of God, in the Christian church, in distinction from the laity; in England, usually restricted to the ministers of the Established Church.
Clerkless : Unlearned.
Clue : That which guides or directs one in anything of a doubtful or intricate nature; that which gives a hint in the solution of a mystery.
Clicker : One who as has charge of the work of a companionship.
Cliff : A series of limestone strata found in Ohio and farther west, presenting bluffs along the rivers and valleys, formerly supposed to be of one formation, but now known to be partly Silurian and partly Devonian.
Climatize : To acclimate or become acclimated.
Climber : A bird that climbs, as a woodpecker or a parrot.
Clinging : of Cling
Clink : To give out a slight, sharp, tinkling sound.
Clinorhombic : Possessing the qualities of a prism, obliquely inclined to a rhombic base; monoclinic.
Clipper : A vessel with a sharp bow, built and rigged for fast sailing.
Cloaked : of Cloak

Croup : An inflammatory affection of the larynx or trachea, accompanied by a hoarse, ringing cough and stridulous, difficult breathing; esp., such an affection when associated with the development of a false membrane in the air passages (also called membranous croup). Crow : A bird, usually black, of the genus Corvus, having a strong conical beak, with projecting bristles. It has a harsh, croaking note. See Caw.

Cryptocrystalline : Indistinctly crystalline; -- applied to rocks and minerals, whose state of aggregation is so fine that no distinct particles are visible, even under the microscope.
Crystal : The regular form which a substance tends to assume in solidifying, through the inherent power of cohesive attraction. It is bounded by plane surfaces, symmetrically arranged, and each species of crystal has fixed axial ratios. See Crystallization.
Crystallize : To be converted into a crystal; to take on a crystalline form, through the action of crystallogenic or cohesive attraction.

Day : The period of the earth's revolution on its axis. -- ordinarily divided into twenty-four hours. It is measured by the interval between two successive transits of a celestial body over the same meridian, and takes a specific name from that of the body. Thus, if this is the sun, the day (the interval between two successive transits of the sun's center over the same meridian) is called a solar day; if it is a star, a sidereal day; if it is the moon, a lunar day. See Civil day, Sidereal day, below.
Day-net : A net for catching small birds.
Dazzlement : Dazzling flash, glare, or burst of light.

Specifically, the conversion of molten glassy matter into a stony mass by slow cooling, the result being the formation of crystallites, microbites, etc., in the glassy base, which are then called devitrification products.

Dextrose : A sirupy, or white crystalline, variety of sugar, C6H12O6 (so called from turning the plane of polarization to the right), occurring in many ripe fruits. Dextrose and levulose are obtained by the inversion of cane sugar or sucrose, and hence called invert sugar. Dextrose is chiefly obtained by the action of heat and acids on starch, and hence called also starch sugar. It is also formed from starchy food by the action of the amylolytic ferments of saliva and pancreatic juice.

Many diseases, of which fever is the most prominent symptom, are denominated fevers; as, typhoid fever; yellow fever.

Flower : That part of a plant destined to produce seed, and hence including one or both of the sexual organs; an organ or combination of the organs of reproduction, whether inclosed by a circle of foliar parts or not. A complete flower consists of two essential parts, the stamens and the pistil, and two floral envelopes, the corolla and callyx. In mosses the flowers consist of a few special leaves surrounding or subtending organs called archegonia. See Blossom, and Corolla.

Function : A quantity so connected with another quantity, that if any alteration be made in the latter there will be a consequent alteration in the former. Each quantity is said to be a function of the other. Thus, the circumference of a circle is a function of the diameter. If x be a symbol to which different numerical values can be assigned, such expressions as x2, 3x, Log. x, and Sin. x, are all functions of x.

Hawthorn : A thorny shrub or tree (the Crataegus oxyacantha), having deeply lobed, shining leaves, small, roselike, fragrant flowers, and a fruit called haw. It is much used in Europe for hedges, and for standards in gardens. The American hawthorn is Crataegus cordata, which has the leaves but little lobed.

Heliometry : The apart or practice of measuring the diameters of heavenly bodies, their relative distances, etc. See Heliometer.
Helix : A nonplane curve whose tangents are all equally inclined to a given plane. The common helix is the curve formed by the thread of the ordinary screw. It is distinguished from the spiral, all the convolutions of which are in the plane.
Hellebore : A genus of perennial herbs (Helleborus) of the Crowfoot family, mostly having powerfully cathartic and even poisonous qualities. H. niger is the European black hellebore, or Christmas rose, blossoming in winter or earliest spring. H. officinalis was the officinal hellebore of the ancients.
Hellespontine : Of or pertaining to the Hellespont.
Helm : A helmet.

Hematemesis : A vomiting of blood.

Hemibranchi : An order of fishes having an incomplete or reduced branchial apparatus. It includes the sticklebacks, the flutemouths, and Fistularia.
Hemimetabolic : Having an incomplete metamorphosis, the larvae differing from the adults chiefly in laking wings, as in the grasshoppers and cockroaches.

Hydatid : A membranous sac or bladder filled with a pellucid fluid, found in various parts of the bodies of animals, but unconnected with the tissues. It is usually formed by parasitic worms, esp. by larval tapeworms, as Echinococcus and Coenurus. See these words in the Vocabulary.
Hydrant : A discharge pipe with a valve and spout at which water may be drawn from the mains of waterworks; a water plug.
Hydrazine : Any one of a series of nitrogenous bases, resembling the amines and produced by the reduction of certain nitroso and diazo compounds; as, methyl hydrazine, phenyl hydrazine, etc. They are derivatives of hydrazine proper, H2N.NH2, which is a doubled amido group, recently (1887) isolated as a stable, colorless gas, with a peculiar, irritating odor. As a base it forms distinct salts. Called also diamide, amidogen, (or more properly diamidogen), etc.
Hydrocarbon : A compound containing only hydrogen and carbon, as methane, benzene, etc.; also, by extension, any of their derivatives.

Hypoderma : A layer of tissue beneath the epidermis in plants, and performing the physiological function of strengthening the epidermal tissue. In phanerogamous plants it is developed as collenchyma.
Hypogynous : Inserted below the pistil or pistils; -- said of sepals, petals, and stamens; having the sepals, petals, and stamens inserted below the pistil; -- said of a flower or a plant.

Ice : Water or other fluid frozen or reduced to the solid state by cold; frozen water. It is a white or transparent colorless substance, crystalline, brittle, and viscoidal. Its specific gravity (0.92, that of water at 4  C. being 1.0) being less than that of water, ice floats.
Iceland : A kind of lichen (Cetraria Icelandica) found from the Arctic regions to the North Temperate zone. It furnishes a nutritious jelly and other forms of food, and is used in pulmonary complaints as a demulcent.

Injector : A contrivance for forcing feed water into a steam boiler by the direct action of the steam upon the water. Inverse : Opposite in nature and effect; -- said with reference to any two operations, which, when both are performed in succession upon any quantity, reproduce that quantity; as, multiplication is the inverse operation to division. The symbol of an inverse operation is the symbol of the direct operation with -1 as an index. Thus sin-1 x means the arc whose sine is x.

The forms J and I have, until a recent time, been classed together, and they have been used interchangeably.

Latex : A milky or colored juice in certain plants in cavities (called latex cells or latex tubes). It contains the peculiar principles of the plants, whether aromatic, bitter, or acid, and in many instances yields caoutchouc upon coagulation.

Lepisma : A genus of wingless thysanurous insects having an elongated flattened body, covered with shining scales and terminated by seven unequal bristles. A common species (Lepisma saccharina) is found in houses, and often injures books and furniture. Called also shiner, silver witch, silver moth, and furniture bug.

Levy : To raise; to collect; said of troops, to form into an army by enrollment, conscription, etc.
Lexicographer : The author or compiler of a lexicon or dictionary.
Leyden : A glass jar or bottle used to accumulate electricity. It is coated with tin foil, within and without, nearly to its top, and is surmounted by a brass knob which communicates with the inner coating, for the purpose of charging it with electricity. It is so named from having been invented in Leyden, Holland.
Lias : The lowest of the three divisions of the Jurassic period; a name given in England and Europe to a series of marine limestones underlying the Oolite. See the Chart of Geology.

Lime : Oxide of calcium; the white or gray, caustic substance, usually called quicklime, obtained by calcining limestone or shells, the heat driving off carbon dioxide and leaving lime. It develops great heat when treated with water, forming slacked lime, and is an essential ingredient of cement, plastering, mortar, etc.

Litchi : The fruit of a tree native to China (Nephelium Litchi). It is nutlike, having a rough but tender shell, containing an aromatic pulp, and a single large seed. In the dried fruit which is exported the pulp somewhat resembles a raisin in color and form.
Literally : With close adherence to words; word by word.
-lite : Combining forms fr. Gr. li`qos a stone; -- used chiefly in naming minerals and rocks.

Lote : A large tree (Celtis australis), found in the south of Europe. It has a hard wood, and bears a cherrylike fruit. Called also nettle tree.

Magnet : The loadstone; a species of iron ore (the ferrosoferric or magnetic ore, Fe3O4) which has the property of attracting iron and some of its ores, and, when freely suspended, of pointing to the poles; -- called also natural magnet.
Magnetite : An oxide of iron (Fe3O4) occurring in isometric crystals, also massive, of a black color and metallic luster. It is readily attracted by a magnet and sometimes possesses polarity, being then called loadstone. It is an important iron ore. Called also magnetic iron.

Mare : Sighing, suffocative panting, intercepted utterance, with a sense of pressure across the chest, occurring during sleep; the incubus; -- obsolete, except in the compound nightmare.
Margay : An American wild cat (Felis tigrina), ranging from Mexico to Brazil. It is spotted with black. Called also long-tailed cat.

Marram : A coarse grass found on sandy beaches (Ammophila arundinacea). See Beach grass, under Beach.

Mars : The god of war and husbandry.
Marshaling : of Marshal
Marsupial : One of the Marsupialia.
Martello : A building of masonry, generally circular, usually erected on the seacoast, with a gun on the summit mounted on a traversing platform, so as to be fired in any direction.
Martinet : In military language, a strict disciplinarian; in general, one who lays stress on a rigid adherence to the details of discipline, or to forms and fixed methods.
Martyrdom : Affliction; torment; torture.
Marvelous : Exciting wonder or surprise; astonishing; wonderful.
Masculine : Having the inflections of, or construed with, words pertaining especially to male beings, as distinguished from feminine and neuter. See Gender.
Mask : A grotesque head or face, used to adorn keystones and other prominent parts, to spout water in fountains, and the like; -- called also mascaron.
Maslach : An excitant containing opium, much used by the Turks.
Masque : A mask; a masquerade.
Mass : The principal part; the main body.
Massiness : The state or quality of being massy; ponderousness.
Master : One who uses, or controls at will, anything inanimate; as, to be master of one's time.
Masterly : Imperious; domineering; arbitrary.
Masthead : The top or head of a mast; the part of a mast above the hounds.
Masticot : Massicot.
Mastology : The natural history of Mammalia.
Matador : In the game of quadrille or omber, the three principal trumps, the ace of spades being the first, the ace of clubs the third, and the second being the deuce of a black trump or the seven of a red one.
Match : To make equal, proportionate, or suitable; to adapt, fit, or suit (one thing to another).
Mate : To confuse; to confound.
Material : The substance or matter of which anything is made or may be made.
Materially : In its essence; substantially.
Mather : See Madder.
Matricide : The murder of a mother by her son or daughter.
Matrix : The five simple colors, black, white, blue, red, and yellow, of which all the rest are composed.
Mattamore : A subterranean repository for wheat.
Matter : To regard as important; to take account of; to care for.
Maturate : To ripen; to become mature; specif/cally, to suppurate.
Maturity : The state or quality of being mature; ripeness; full development; as, the maturity of corn or of grass; maturity of judgment; the maturity of a plan.
Maukin : See Malkin.
Maunderer : One who maunders.
Maw : An old game at cards.
Maxilla : One of the lower or outer jaws of arthropods.
May : An auxiliary verb qualifyng the meaning of another verb, by expressing: (a) Ability, competency, or possibility; -- now oftener expressed by can.
Maying : The celebrating of May Day.
Maze : A wild fancy; a confused notion.
Meach : To skulk; to cower. See Mich.
Meagreness : The state or quality of being meager; leanness; scantiness; barrenness.
Mean : To signify; to indicate; to import; to denote.
Meander : To wind, turn, or twist; to make flexuous.
Meanwhile : In the intervening time; during the interval.
Measure : Extent or degree not excessive or beyong bounds; moderation; due restraint; esp. in the phrases, in measure; with measure; without or beyond measure.
Measure : To make a measurement or measurements.
Meatoscope : A speculum for examining a natural passage, as the urethra.
Mechanical : Of or pertaining to a machine or to machinery or tools; made or formed by a machine or with tools; as, mechanical precision; mechanical products.
Mechanographic : Treating of mechanics.
Medaling : of Medal
Meddlingly : In a meddling manner.
Mediastine : Alt. of Mediastinum
Mediator : One who mediates; especially, one who interposes between parties at variance for the purpose of reconciling them; hence, an intercessor.
Medicative : Medicinal; acting like a medicine.
Medina : A subdivision of the Niagara period in the American upper Silurian, characterized by the formations known as the Oneida conglomerate, and the Medina sandstone. See the Chart of Geology.
Meditatist : One who is given to meditation.
Medle : To mix; to mingle; to meddle.
Medullin : A variety of lignin or cellulose found in the medulla, or pith, of certain plants. Cf. Lignin, and Cellulose.
Meekly : In a meek manner.
Meet : Suitable; fit; proper; appropriate; qualified; convenient.
Megacosm : See Macrocosm.
Megameter : An instrument for determining longitude by observation of the stars.
Megatheroid : One of a family of extinct edentates found in America. The family includes the megatherium, the megalonyx, etc.
Meistersinger : See Mastersinger.
Melancholily : In a melancholy manner.
Melanin : A black pigment found in the pigment-bearing cells of the skin (particularly in the skin of the negro), in the epithelial cells of the external layer of the retina (then called fuscin), in the outer layer of the choroid, and elsewhere. It is supposed to be derived from the decomposition of hemoglobin.
Melasses : See Molasses.
Melicratory : A meadlike drink.
Melissic : Pertaining to, or derived from, beeswax; specif., denoting an acid obtained by oxidation of myricin.
Melliphagan : See Meliphagan.
Melluco : A climbing plant (Ullucus officinalis) of the Andes, having tuberous roots which are used as a substitute for potatoes.
Melodies : of Melody
Melting : of Melt
Member : One of the persons composing a society, community, or the like; an individual forming part of an association; as, a member of the society of Friends.
Memoirs : A memorial account; a history composed from personal experience and memory; an account of transactions or events (usually written in familiar style) as they are remembered by the writer. See History, 2.
Memorial : A species of informal state paper, much used in negotiation.
Men : pl. of Man.
Mended : of Mend
Mendinant : A mendicant or begging friar.
Meningitis : Inflammation of the membranes of the brain or spinal cord.
Menology : A brief calendar of the lives of the saints for each day in the year, or a simple remembrance of those whose lives are not written.
Menstruated : of Menstruate
Mental : Of or pertaining to the chin; genian; as, the mental nerve; the mental region.
Menu : The details of a banquet; a bill of fare.
Merce : To subject to fine or amercement; to mulct; to amerce.
Merchandiser : A trader.
Mercurial : Having the qualities fabled to belong to the god Mercury; swift; active; sprightly; fickle; volatile; changeable; as, a mercurial youth; a mercurial temperament.
Mercurify : To obtain mercury from, as mercuric minerals, which may be done by any application of intense heat that expels the mercury in fumes, which are afterward condensed.
Mere : To divide, limit, or bound.
Meride : A permanent colony of cells or plastids which may remain isolated, like Rotifer, or may multiply by gemmation to form higher aggregates, termed zoides.
Meristem : A tissue of growing cells, or cells capable of further division.
Merkin : Originally, a wig; afterwards, a mop for cleaning cannon.
Merostomata : A class of Arthropoda, allied to the Crustacea. It includes the trilobites, Eurypteroidea, and Limuloidea. All are extinct except the horseshoe crabs of the last group. See Limulus.
Merrymeeting : A meeting for mirth.
Meseemed : of Meseems
Mesh : To engage with each other, as the teeth of wheels.
Mesmerizer : One who mesmerizes.
Mesocoelia : The cavity of the mesencephalon; the iter.
Mesohippus : An extinct mammal of the Horse family, but not larger than a sheep, and having three toes on each foot.
Mesopodium : The middle portion of the foot in the Gastropoda and Pteropoda.
Mesothorax : The middle segment of the thorax in insects. See Illust. of Coleoptera.
Messing : of Mess
Messinese : Of or pertaining to Messina, or its inhabitans.
Metabases : of Metabasis
Metacetone : A colorless liquid of an agreeable odor, C6H10O, obtained by distilling a mixture of sugar and lime; -- so called because formerly regarded as a polymeric modification of acetone.
Metal : An elementary substance, as sodium, calcium, or copper, whose oxide or hydroxide has basic rather than acid properties, as contrasted with the nonmetals, or metalloids. No sharp line can be drawn between the metals and nonmetals, and certain elements partake of both acid and basic qualities, as chromium, manganese, bismuth, etc.
Metaleptic : Of or pertaining to a metalepsis.
Metallochromy : The art or process of coloring metals.
Metalogical : Beyond the scope or province of logic.
Metamorphosic : Changing the form; transforming.
Metaphosphoric : Pertaining to, or designating, a monobasic acid, HPO3, analogous to nitric acid, and, by heating phosphoric acid, obtained as a crystalline substance, commonly called glacial phosphoric acid.
Metapode : The posterior division of the foot in the Gastropoda and Pteropoda.
Metasternal : Of or pertaining to the metasternum.
Metatungstic : Of, pertaining to, or designating, an acid known only in its salts (the metatungstates) and properly called polytungstic, or pyrotungstic, acid.
Mete : Measure; limit; boundary; -- used chiefly in the plural, and in the phrase metes and bounds.
Meteorism : Flatulent distention of the abdomen; tympanites.
Meter : An instrument for measuring, and usually for recording automatically, the quantity measured.
Methionate : A salt of methionic acid.
Methodizing : of Methodize
Metis : Alt. of Metisse
Metric : Of or pertaining to the meter as a standard of measurement; of or pertaining to the decimal system of measurement of which a meter is the unit; as, the metric system; a metric measurement.
Metropole : A metropolis.
Mettlesome : Full of spirit; possessing constitutional ardor; fiery; as, a mettlesome horse.
Mexican : Of or pertaining to Mexico or its people.
Mezzotint : To engrave in mezzotint.
Miauled : of Miaul
Micraster : A genus of sea urchins, similar to Spatangus, abounding in the chalk formation; -- from the starlike disposal of the ambulacral furrows.
Micrococci : of Micrococcus
Microhm : The millionth part of an ohm.

Microscopic : Alt. of Microscopical
Microzoa : The Infusoria.
Midding : Same as Midden.
Midfeather : A vertical water space in a fire box or combustion chamber.
Midrib : A continuation of the petiole, extending from the base to the apex of the lamina of a leaf.
Midway : Being in the middle of the way or distance; as, the midway air.
Mightiness : Highness; excellency; -- with a possessive pronoun, a title of dignity; as, their high mightinesses.
Migration : The act of migrating.
Mileage : An allowance for traveling expenses at a certain rate per mile.
Militancy : A military spirit or system; militarism.
Milk : An emulsion made by bruising seeds; as, the milk of almonds, produced by pounding almonds with sugar and water.
Milkweed : Any plant of the genera Asclepias and Acerates, abounding in a milky juice, and having its seed attached to a long silky down; silkweed. The name is also applied to several other plants with a milky juice, as to several kinds of spurge.
Mill : To shape, finish, or transform by passing through a machine; specifically, to shape or dress, as metal, by means of a rotary cutter.
Millenniarism : Belief in, or expectation of, the millennium; millenarianism.
Milliaries : of Milliary
Millionairess : A woman who is a millionaire, or the wife of a millionaire.
Milt : The spleen.
Mimetism : Same as Mimicry.
Minas : of Mina
Mince-meat : Minced meat; meat chopped very fine; a mixture of boiled meat, suet, apples, etc., chopped very fine, to which spices and raisins are added; -- used in making mince pie.
Minder : One to be attended; specif., a pauper child intrusted to the care of a private person.
Miner : Any of numerous insects which, in the larval state, excavate galleries in the parenchyma of leaves. They are mostly minute moths and dipterous flies.
Mineralogist : A carrier shell (Phorus).
Mingledly : Confusedly.
Minibus : A kind of light passenger vehicle, carrying four persons.
Minimized : of Minimize
Minionlike : Alt. of Minionly
Ministerially : In a ministerial manner; in the character or capacity of a minister.
Minnow : A small European fresh-water cyprinoid fish (Phoxinus laevis, formerly Leuciscus phoxinus); sometimes applied also to the young of larger kinds; -- called also minim and minny. The name is also applied to several allied American species, of the genera Phoxinus, Notropis, or Minnilus, and Rhinichthys.
Minster : A church of a monastery. The name is often retained and applied to the church after the monastery has ceased to exist (as Beverly Minster, Southwell Minster, etc.), and is also improperly used for any large church.
Minuet : A tune or air to regulate the movements of the dance so called; a movement in suites, sonatas, symphonies, etc., having the dance form, and commonly in 3-4, sometimes 3-8, measure.
Minute-jack : A figure which strikes the hour on the bell of some fanciful clocks; -- called also jack of the clock house.
Mira : A remarkable variable star in the constellation Cetus (/ Ceti).
Mired : of Mire
Mirth : That which causes merriment.
Misaffected : Ill disposed.
Misappreciated : Improperly appreciated.
Misboden : of Misbede
Miscalculate : To calculate erroneously; to judge wrongly.
Miscellanies : of Miscellany
Mischna : See Mishna.
Miscompute : To compute erroneously.
Misconstrued : of Misconstrue
Miscreate : To create badly or amiss.
Misdepart : To distribute wrongly.
Misdo : To do wrong to; to illtreat.

Misericordia : An amercement.

Misguidance : Wrong guidance.
Misinform : To give untrue information to; to inform wrongly.
Miskin : A little bagpipe.
Milen : See Maslin.
Mismate : To mate wrongly or unsuitably; as, to mismate gloves or shoes; a mismated couple.
Misorder : Irregularity; disorder.
Mispoint : To point improperly; to punctuate wrongly.
Misproud : Viciously proud.
Misrelate : To relate inaccurately.
Miss : A young unmarried woman or a girl; as, she is a miss of sixteen.
Missay : To say wrongly.
Missingly : With a sense of loss.
Missound : To sound wrongly; to utter or pronounce incorrectly.
Missuccess : Failure.
Mistake : To substitute in thought or perception; as, to mistake one person for another.
Mister : A title of courtesy prefixed to the name of a man or youth. It is usually written in the abbreviated form Mr.
Mistily : With mist; darkly; obscurely.
Mistress : A woman regarded with love and devotion; she who has command over one's heart; a beloved object; a sweetheart.
Mistura : Sometimes, a liquid medicine containing very active substances, and which can only be administered by drops.
Misvalue : To value wrongly or too little; to undervalue.
Mite : A small weight; one twentieth of a grain.
Mitigable : Admitting of mitigation; that may be mitigated.
Mitten : A covering for the hand, worn to defend it from cold or injury. It differs from a glove in not having a separate sheath for each finger.
Mixedly : In a mixed or mingled manner.
Mizzled : of Mizzle
Moan : To make a low prolonged sound of grief or pain, whether articulate or not; to groan softly and continuously.
Mobile : Characterized by an extreme degree of fluidity; moving or flowing with great freedom; as, benzine and mercury are mobile liquids; -- opposed to viscous, viscoidal, or oily.
Mocha : A variety of coffee brought from Mocha.
Mocker : One who, or that which, mocks; a scorner; a scoffer; a derider.
Mode : Prevailing popular custom; fashion, especially in the phrase the mode.
Modeler : One who models; hence, a worker in plastic art.
Moderated : of Moderate
Moderatrix : A female moderator.
Modicity : Moderateness; smallness; meanness.
Modiste : A female maker of, or dealer in, articles of fashion, especially of the fashionable dress of ladies; a woman who gives direction to the style or mode of dress.
Modus : The arrangement of, or mode of expressing, the terms of a contract or conveyance.
Mohammedan : A follower of Mohammed, the founder of Islamism; one who professes Mohammedanism or Islamism.
Moiety : An indefinite part; a small part.
Moistful : Full of moisture.
Mold : A spot; a blemish; a mole.
Mould : A group of moldings; as, the arch mold of a porch or doorway; the pier mold of a Gothic pier, meaning the whole profile, section, or combination of parts.
Moulder : To crumble into small particles; to turn to dust by natural decay; to lose form, or waste away, by a gradual separation of the component particles, without the presence of water; to crumble away.
Mole : A mound or massive work formed of masonry or large stones, etc., laid in the sea, often extended either in a right line or an arc of a circle before a port which it serves to defend from the violence of the waves, thus protecting ships in a harbor; also, sometimes, the harbor itself.
Moleskin : Any fabric having a thick soft shag, like the fur of a mole; esp., a kind of strong twilled fustian.
Mollient : Serving to soften; assuaging; emollient.
Molluscoidea : A division of Invertebrata which includes the classes Brachiopoda and Bryozoa; -- called also Anthoid Mollusca.
Molt : Alt. of Moult
Moment : Impulsive power; force; momentum.
Momentum : Essential element, or constituent element.
Monadical : Of, pertaining to, or like, a monad, in any of its senses. See Monad, n.
Monarchial : Monarchic.
Monastic : A monk.
Moneral : Of or pertaining to the Monera.
Moneyage : Mintage; coinage.
Mongolian : One of the Mongols.
Monism : See Monogenesis, 1.
Monitrix : A female monitor.
Monkey's : "A lofty coniferous Chilian tree (Araucaria imbricata), the branches of which are so crowded and intertwisted ""as to puzzle a monkey to climb."" The edible nuts are over an inch long, and are called pi on by the Chilians."
Monocarpellary : Consisting of a single carpel, as the fruit of the pea, cherry, and almond.
Monocotyl : Any monocotyledonous plant.
Monodical : Belonging to a monody.
Monogamian : Alt. of Monogamic
Monogenous : Of or pertaining to monogenesis; as, monogenous, or asexual, reproduction.
Monogynia : A Linnaean order of plants, including those which have only one style or stigma.
Monomania : Derangement of the mind in regard of a single subject only; also, such a concentration of interest upon one particular subject or train of ideas to show mental derangement.
Monomyary : Of or pertaining to the Monomya.
Monoplegia : Paralysis affecting a single limb.
Monopoly : The commodity or other material thing to which the monopoly relates; as, tobacco is a monopoly in France.
Monostrophic : Having one strophe only; not varied in measure; written in unvaried measure.
Monothelite : One of an ancient sect who held that Christ had but one will as he had but one nature. Cf. Monophysite.
Monovalent : Having a valence of one; univalent. See Univalent.
Monster : Specifically , an animal or plant departing greatly from the usual type, as by having too many limbs.
Montanic : Of or pertaining to mountains; consisting of mountains.
Monthly : As if under the influence of the moon; in the manner of a lunatic.
Moo : See Mo.
Moon : A secondary planet, or satellite, revolving about any member of the solar system; as, the moons of Jupiter or Saturn.
Moon-eyed : Having eyes affected by the moon; moonblind; dim-eyed; purblind.
Moonset : The descent of the moon below the horizon; also, the time when the moon sets.
Moor : Any individual of the swarthy races of Africa or Asia which have adopted the Mohammedan religion.
Mooruk : A species of cassowary (Casuarius Bennetti) found in New Britain, and noted for its agility in running and leaping. It is smaller and has stouter legs than the common cassowary. Its crest is biloted; the neck and breast are black; the back, rufous mixed with black; and the naked skin of the neck, blue.
Moot-hill : A hill of meeting or council; an elevated place in the open air where public assemblies or courts were held by the Saxons; -- called, in Scotland, mute-hill.
Moplah : One of a class of Mohammedans in Malabar.
Moral : Serving to teach or convey a moral; as, a moral lesson; moral tales.
Moralizing : of Moralize
Morbid : Of or pertaining to disease or diseased parts; as, morbid anatomy.
Mordant : Any sticky matter by which the gold leaf is made to adhere.
More : With an adjective or adverb (instead of the suffix -er) to form the comparative degree; as, more durable; more active; more sweetly.
Morgue : A place where the bodies of persons found dead are exposed, that they may be identified, or claimed by their friends; a deadhouse.
Morioplasty : The restoration of lost parts of the body.
Morne : Without teeth, tongue, or claws; -- said of a lion represented heraldically.
Moroshop : A philosophical or learned fool.
Morphophyly : The tribal history of forms; that part of phylogeny which treats of the tribal history of forms, in distinction from the tribal history of functions.
Morse : A telegraphic alphabet in very general use, inventing by Samuel F.B.Morse, the inventor of Morse's telegraph. The letters are represented by dots and dashes impressed or printed on paper, as, .- (A), - . . . (B), -.. (D), . (E), .. (O), . . . (R), -- (T), etc., or by sounds, flashes of light, etc., with greater or less intervals between them.
Mortality : The condition or quality of being mortal; subjection to death or to the necessity of dying.
Mortgaging : of Mortgage
Mortify : To destroy the organic texture and vital functions of; to produce gangrene in.
Mortpay : Dead pay; the crime of taking pay for the service of dead soldiers, or for services not actually rendered by soldiers.
Mosaism : Attachment to the system or doctrines of Moses; that which is peculiar to the Mosaic system or doctrines.
Moss : A cryptogamous plant of a cellular structure, with distinct stem and simple leaves. The fruit is a small capsule usually opening by an apical lid, and so discharging the spores. There are many species, collectively termed Musci, growing on the earth, on rocks, and trunks of trees, etc., and a few in running water.
Mostick : A painter's maul-stick.
Mote : A body of persons who meet for discussion, esp. about the management of affairs; as, a folkmote.
Mothered : of Mother
Mothy : Infested with moths; moth-eaten.
Motion : To propose; to move.
Motmot : Any one of several species of long-tailed, passerine birds of the genus Momotus, having a strong serrated beak. In most of the species the two long middle tail feathers are racket-shaped at the tip, when mature. The bird itself is said by some writers to trim them into this shape. They feed on insects, reptiles, and fruit, and are found from Mexico to Brazil. The name is derived from its note.
Mottoed : Bearing or having a motto; as, a mottoed coat or device.
Mound : A ball or globe forming part of the regalia of an emperor or other sovereign. It is encircled with bands, enriched with precious stones, and surmounted with a cross; -- called also globe.
Mount : The cardboard or cloth on which a drawing, photograph, or the like is mounted; a mounting.
Mountebank : To cheat by boasting and false pretenses; to gull.
Mourn : To utter in a mournful manner or voice.
Mouse : To watch for and catch mice.
Mousy : Infested with mice; smelling of mice.
Mouth : To make mouths at.
Movable : An article of wares or goods; a commodity; a piece of property not fixed, or not a part of real estate; generally, in the plural, goods; wares; furniture.
Movement : The act of moving; change of place or posture; transference, by any means, from one situation to another; natural or appropriate motion; progress; advancement; as, the movement of an army in marching or maneuvering; the movement of a wheel or a machine; the party of movement.
Mow : of Mow
Mowing : The act of one who, or the operation of that which, mows.
Mucedin : A yellowish white, amorphous, nitrogenous substance found in wheat, rye, etc., and resembling gluten; -- formerly called also mucin.
Mucilaginous : Of, pertaining to, or secreting, mucilage; as, the mucilaginous glands.
Muckmidden : A dunghill.
Muculent : Slimy; moist, and moderately viscous.
Muddle : To think and act in a confused, aimless way.
Mudhole : A hole near the bottom, through which the sediment is withdrawn.
Muffish : Stupid; awkward.
Mug : A kind of earthen or metal drinking cup, with a handle, -- usually cylindrical and without a lip.
Muhammedan : Mohammedan.
Mulct : Hence, to deprive of; to withhold by way of punishment or discipline.
Mulierty : Condition of being a mulier; position of one born in lawful wedlock.
Muller : A vessel in which wine, etc., is mulled over a fire.
Mulliod : Like or pertaining to the genus Mullus, which includes the surmullet, or red mullet.
Multicuspidate : Having many cusps or points.
Multigranulate : Having, or consisting of, many grains.
Multiparous : Producing many, or more than one, at a birth.
Multiplier : One who, or that which, multiplies or increases number.
Multiseptate : Divided into many chambers by partitions, as the pith of the pokeweed.
Multivalent : Having more than one degree of valence, as sulphur.
Mumble : To speak with the lips partly closed, so as to render the sounds inarticulate and imperfect; to utter words in a grumbling indistinct manner, indicating discontent or displeasure; to mutter.
Mummification : The act of making a mummy.
Mump : To be sullen or sulky.
Mundatory : Cleansing; having power to cleanse.
Mungrel : See Mongrel.
Munjeet : See Indian madder, under Madder.
Murderer : A small cannon, formerly used for clearing a ship's decks of boarders; -- called also murdering piece.
Muricate : Alt. of Muricated
Murmur : To make a low continued noise, like the hum of bees, a stream of water, distant waves, or the wind in a forest.
Murry : See Muraena.
Muscadine : See Muscardin.
Muscle : See Mussel.
Musculation : The muscular system of an animal, or of any of its parts.
Muse : Contemplation which abstracts the mind from passing scenes; absorbing thought; hence, absence of mind; a brown study.
Music : Harmony; an accordant combination of simultaneous tones.
Musk : A plant of the genus Muscari; grape hyacinth.
Muskwood : The wood of an Australian tree (Eurybia argophylla).
Mussel : Any one of numerous species of Unio, and related fresh-water genera; -- called also river mussel. See Naiad, and Unio.
Mustachios : of Mustacho
Mustiness : The quality or state of being musty.
Mute : Incapable of speaking; dumb.
Mutilate : To cut off or remove a limb or essential part of; to maim; to cripple; to hack; as, to mutilate the body, a statue, etc.
Mutter : To utter words indistinctly or with a low voice and lips partly closed; esp., to utter indistinct complaints or angry expressions; to grumble; to growl.
Mux : To mix in an unitidy and offensive way; to make a mess of.
Myaria : A division of bivalve mollusks of which the common clam (Mya) is the type.
Mydriatic : A mydriatic medicine or agent, as belladonna.
Mylodon : An extinct genus of large slothlike American edentates, allied to Megatherium.
Myograph : An instrument for determining and recording the different phases, as the intensity, velocity, etc., of a muscular contraction.
Myophan : A contractile striated layer found in the bodies and stems of certain Infusoria.
Myriacanthous : Having numerous spines, as certain fishes.
Myriophyllous : Having an indefinitely great or countless number of leaves.
Myrrhic : Of, pertaining to, or obtained from, myrrh.
Mysteriousness : Something mysterious; a mystery.
Mystification : The act of mystifying, or the state of being mystied; also, something designed to, or that does, mystify.
Mythologizer : One who, or that which, mythologizes.
Myzostomata : An order of curious parasitic worms found on crinoids. The body is short and disklike, with four pairs of suckers and five pairs of hook-bearing parapodia on the under side.
Nadde : Had not.

Naked : Without pubescence; as, a naked leaf or stem; bare, or not covered by the customary parts, as a flower without a perianth, a stem without leaves, seeds without a pericarp, buds without bud scales.

Narrow : To lessen the breadth of; to contract; to draw into a smaller compass; to reduce the width or extent of.

Natant : Floating in water, as the leaves of water lilies, or submersed, as those of many aquatic plants.
Natica : Any one of numerous species of marine gastropods belonging to Natica, Lunatia, Neverita, and other allied genera (family Naticidae.) They burrow beneath the sand, or mud, and drill other shells.

Navies : of Navvy
Nazarite : A Jew bound by a vow to lave the hair uncut, to abstain from wine and strong drink, and to practice extraordinary purity of life and devotion, the obligation being for life, or for a certain time. The word is also used adjectively.
Near : Not far distant in time, place, or degree; not remote; close at hand; adjacent; neighboring; nigh.

Negativity : The quality or state of being negative.
Negligence : The omission of the care usual under the circumstances, being convertible with the Roman culpa. A specialist is bound to higher skill and diligence in his specialty than one who is not a specialist, and liability for negligence varies acordingly.

Neodymium : An elementary substance which forms one of the constituents of didymium. Symbol Nd. Atomic weight 140.8.
Neologization : The act or process of neologizing.
Neoplatonism : A pantheistic eclectic school of philosophy, of which Plotinus was the chief (A. D. 205-270), and which sought to reconcile the Platonic and Aristotelian systems with Oriental theosophy. It tended to mysticism and theurgy, and was the last product of Greek philosophy.
Nepenthe : A drug used by the ancients to give relief from pain and sorrow; -- by some supposed to have been opium or hasheesh. Hence, anything soothing and comforting.
Nephrite : A hard compact mineral, of a dark green color, formerly worn as a remedy for diseases of the kidneys, whence its name; kidney stone; a kind of jade. See Jade.
Neptunist : One who adopts the neptunian theory.
Neroli : An essential oil obtained by distillation from the flowers of the orange. It has a strong odor, and is used in perfumery, etc.
Nervimotion : The movement caused in the sensory organs by external agents and transmitted to the muscles by the nerves.

Neurokeratin : A substance, resembling keratin, present in nerve tissue, as in the sheath of the axis cylinder of medullated nerve fibers. Like keratin it resists the action of most chemical agents, and by decomposition with sulphuric acid yields leucin and tyrosin.

Nicker : A rounded seed, rather smaller than a nutmeg, having a hard smooth shell, and a yellowish or bluish color. The seeds grow in the prickly pods of tropical, woody climbers of the genus Caesalpinia. C. Bonduc has yellowish seeds; C. Bonducella, bluish gray.

Primogeniture : The exclusive right of inheritance which belongs to the eldest son. Thus in England the right of inheriting the estate of the father belongs to the eldest son, and in the royal family the eldest son of the sovereign is entitled to the throne by primogeniture. In exceptional cases, among the female children, the crown descends by right of primogeniture to the eldest daughter only and her issue.

Protocol : An agreement of diplomatists indicating the results reached by them at a particular stage of a negotiation.
Protoplasm : "The viscid and more or less granular material of vegetable and animal cells, possessed of vital properties by which the processes of nutrition, secretion, and growth go forward; the so-called "" physical basis of life;"" the original cell substance, cytoplasm, cytoblastema, bioplasm sarcode, etc."
Protovertebra : One of the primitive masses, or segments, into which the mesoblast of the vertebrate embryo breaks up on either side of the anterior part of the notochord; a mesoblastic, or protovertebral, somite. See Illust. of Ectoderm.

Proudling : A proud or haughty person.

Proverb : A familiar illustration; a subject of contemptuous reference.
Provide : To procure supplies or means in advance; to take measures beforehand in view of an expected or a possible future need, especially a danger or an evil; -- followed by against or for; as, to provide against the inclemency of the weather; to provide for the education of a child.
Provincial : Exhibiting the ways or manners of a province; characteristic of the inhabitants of a province; not cosmopolitan; countrified; not polished; rude; hence, narrow; illiberal.

Pseudo-china : The false china root, a plant of the genus Smilax (S. Pseudo-china), found in America.

Psychical : Of or pertaining to the mind, or its functions and diseases; mental; -- contrasted with physical.

Pterobranchia : An order of marine Bryozoa, having a bilobed lophophore and an axial cord. The genus Rhabdopleura is the type. Called also Podostomata. See Rhabdopleura.

Ptisan : An aqueous medicine, containing little, if any, medicinal agent; a tea or tisane.

Puncheon : A cask containing, sometimes 84, sometimes 120, gallons.
Punctual : Appearing or done at, or adhering exactly to, a regular or an appointed time; precise; prompt; as, a punctual man; a punctual payment.

Purpuric : Pertaining to or designating, a nitrogenous acid contained in uric acid. It is not known in the pure state, but forms well-known purple-red compounds (as murexide), whence its name.

Putlog : One of the short pieces of timber on which the planks forming the floor of a scaffold are laid, -- one end resting on the ledger of the scaffold, and the other in a hole left in the wall temporarily for the purpose.

Pygropodes : A division of swimming birds which includes the grebes, divers, auks, etc., in which the legs are placed far back.
Pyocyanin : A blue coloring matter found in the pus from old sores, supposed to be formed through the agency of a species of bacterium (Bacillus pyocyaneus).
Pyramidoid : A solid resembling a pyramid; -- called also pyramoid.
Pyrexical : Of or pertaining to fever; feverish.
Pyro- : Alt. of Pyr-
Pyrogallol : A phenol metameric with phloroglucin, obtained by the distillation of gallic acid as a poisonous white crystalline substance having acid properties, and hence called also pyrogallic acid. It is a strong reducer, and is used as a developer in photography and in the production of certain dyes.
Pyromancy : Divination by means of fire.
Pyrophorus : Any one of several substances or mixtures which phosphoresce or ignite spontaneously on exposure to air, as a heated mixture of alum, potash, and charcoal, or a mixture of charcoal and finely divided lead.
Pyrothonide : A kind of empyreumatic oil produced by the combustion of textures of hemp, linen, or cotton in a copper vessel, -- formerly used as a remedial agent.

Quick : Speedy; hasty; swift; not slow; as, be quick.
Quickening : The first motion of the fetus in the womb felt by the mother, occurring usually about the middle of the term of pregnancy. It has been popularly supposed to be due to the fetus becoming possessed of independent life.
Quick-witted : Having ready wit
Quidnunc : One who is curious to know everything that passes; one who knows, or pretends to know, all that is going on.

Quinine : An alkaloid extracted from the bark of several species of cinchona (esp. Cinchona Calisaya) as a bitter white crystalline substance, C20H24N2O2. Hence, by extension (Med.), any of the salts of this alkaloid, as the acetate, chloride, sulphate, etc., employed as a febrifuge or antiperiodic. Called also quinia, quinina, etc.
Quinquangular : Having five angles or corners.
Quinquepartite : Consisting of five parts.

Radius : An ideal straight line joining the center of an attracting body with that of a body describing an orbit around it, as a line joining the sun and a planet or comet, or a planet and its satellite.
Raffle : A kind of lottery, in which several persons pay, in shares, the value of something put up as a stake, and then determine by chance (as by casting dice) which one of them shall become the sole possessor.

Regulator : A contrivance for regulating and controlling motion, as: (a) The lever or index in a watch, which controls the effective length of the hairspring, and thus regulates the vibrations of the balance. (b) The governor of a steam engine. (c) A valve for controlling the admission of steam to the steam chest, in a locomotive.

Remote : Removed to a distance; not near; far away; distant; -- said in respect to time or to place; as, remote ages; remote lands.

Renegade : An apostate from Christianity or from any form of religious faith.
Renewal : The act of renewing, or the state of being renewed; as, the renewal of a treaty.
Rennin : A milk-clotting enzyme obtained from the true stomach (abomasum) of a suckling calf. Mol. wt. about 31,000. Also called chymosin, rennase, and abomasal enzyme.
Renown : The state of being much known and talked of; exalted reputation derived from the extensive praise of great achievements or accomplishments; fame; celebrity; -- always in a good sense.
Rent : To take and hold under an agreement to pay rent; as, the tennant rents an estate of the owner.
Renverse : Reversed; set with the head downward; turned contrary to the natural position.
Repace : To pace again; to walk over again in a contrary direction.
Repand : Having a slightly undulating margin; -- said of leaves.
Repast : That which is taken as food; a meal; figuratively, any refreshment.
Repeal : Revocation; abrogation; as, the repeal of a statute; the repeal of a law or a usage.
Repeater : A pennant used to indicate that a certain flag in a hoist of signal is duplicated.
Repent : To change the mind, or the course of conduct, on account of regret or dissatisfaction.
Repercussion : The subsidence of a tumor or eruption by the action of a repellent.
Repetitionary : Of the nature of, or containing, repetition.
Replacement : The act of replacing.
Repletion : Fullness of blood; plethora.
Replication : The reply of the plaintiff, in matters of fact, to the defendant's plea.
Report : To give an account of; to relate; to tell; to circulate publicly, as a story; as, in the common phrase, it is reported.

Reposed : Composed; calm; tranquil; at rest.

Representatively : In a representative manner; vicariously.

Reproacher : One who reproaches.
Reprobatory : Reprobative.

Republic : A state in which the sovereign power resides in the whole body of the people, and is exercised by representatives elected by them; a commonwealth. Cf. Democracy, 2.
Repudiated : of Repudiate
Repulse : To repel; to beat or drive back; as, to repulse an assault; to repulse the enemy.

Reseda : A grayish green color, like that of the flowers of mignonette.

Resentingly : With a sense of wrong or affront; with resentment.

Resiniform : Having the form of resin.
Resistant : Making resistance; resisting.
Resolution : The state of being relaxed; relaxation.
Resolve : To express, as an opinion or determination, by resolution and vote; to declare or decide by a formal vote; -- followed by a clause; as, the house resolved (or, it was resolved by the house) that no money should be apropriated (or, to appropriate no money).
Resolver : That which decomposes, or dissolves.
Resort : The act of going to, or making application; a betaking one's self; the act of visiting or seeking; recourse; as, a place of popular resort; -- often figuratively; as, to have resort to force.
Resourceless : Destitute of resources.
Respectable : Worthy of respect; fitted to awaken esteem; deserving regard; hence, of good repute; not mean; as, a respectable citizen.
