Response : A repetition of the given subject in a fugue by another part on the fifth above or fourth below.
Rest : To arrest.
Rest : To lay or place at rest; to quiet.

Reticulate : Alt. of Reticulated
Retinasphalt : Alt. of Retinasphaltum
Retirade : A kind of retrenchment, as in the body of a bastion, which may be disputed inch by inch after the defenses are dismantled. It usually consists of two faces which make a reentering angle.
Retistene : A white crystalline hydrocarbon produced indirectly from retene.
Retoucher : One who retouches.
Retraction : The state or condition of a part when drawn back, or towards the center of the body.
Retreat : A period of several days of withdrawal from society to a religious house for exclusive occupation in the duties of devotion; as, to appoint or observe a retreat.
Retribution : Specifically, reward and punishment, as distributed at the general judgment.
Retroaction : Action returned, or action backward.

Retrorse : Bent backward or downward.
Rette : See Aret.
Return : Hence, to elect according to the official report of the election officers.

Rhetorician : Suitable to a master of rhetoric.
Rhine : A water course; a ditch.
Rhinophore : One of the two tentacle-like organs on the back of the head or neck of a nudibranch or tectibranch mollusk. They are usually retractile, and often transversely furrowed or plicate, and are regarded as olfactory organs. Called also dorsal tentacles. See Illust. under Pygobranchia, and Opisthobranchia.
Rhizoid : A rootlike appendage.
Rhodian : Of or pertaining to Rhodes, an island of the Mediterranean.
Rhombogene : A dicyemid which produces infusorialike embryos; -- opposed to nematogene. See Dicyemata.
Rhotacism : An oversounding, or a misuse, of the letter r; specifically (Phylol.), the tendency, exhibited in the Indo-European languages, to change s to r, as wese to were.
Rhymery : The art or habit of making rhymes; rhyming; -- in contempt.
Rhythmic : Alt. of Rhythmical
Rib : The chief nerve, or one of the chief nerves, of a leaf.

Ribboning : of Ribbon
Rich : Hence, in general, well supplied; abounding; abundant; copious; bountiful; as, a rich treasury; a rich entertainment; a rich crop.
Ricinoleic : Pertaining to, or designating, a fatty acid analogous to oleic acid, obtained from castor oil as an oily substance, C/H/O/ with a harsh taste. Formerly written ricinolic.
Rictus : The gape of the mouth, as of birds; -- often resricted to the corners of the mouth.
Riddle : Something proposed to be solved by guessing or conjecture; a puzzling question; an ambiguous proposition; an enigma; hence, anything ambiguous or puzzling.

Rigidity : The quality or state of being rigid; want of pliability; the quality of resisting change of form; the amount of resistance with which a body opposes change of form; -- opposed to flexibility, ductility, malleability, and softness.
Rigorism : Rigidity in principle or practice; strictness; -- opposed to laxity.
Rim : The border, edge, or margin of a thing, usually of something circular or curving; as, the rim of a kettle or basin.
Rimmer : An implement for cutting, trimming, or ornamenting the rim of anything, as the edges of pies, etc.; also, a reamer.

River : To hawk by the side of a river; to fly hawks at river fowl.
Rixdaler : A Dutch silver coin, worth about $1.00.

Roar : To bellow, or utter a deep, loud cry, as a lion or other beast.

Rob : To deprive of, or withhold from, unjustly or injuriously; to defraud; as, to rob one of his rest, or of his good name; a tree robs the plants near it of sunlight.
Robin : An American singing bird (Merula migratoria), having the breast chestnut, or dull red. The upper parts are olive-gray, the head and tail blackish. Called also robin redbreast, and migratory thrush.
Robustness : The quality or state of being robust.
Rock : The striped bass. See under Bass.
Rocket : Damewort.
Rock : A shaft that oscillates on its journals, instead of revolving, -- usually carrying levers by means of which it receives and communicates reciprocating motion, as in the valve gear of some steam engines; -- called also rocker, rocking shaft, and way shaft.
Roddy : Full of rods or twigs.

Roin : A scab; a scurf, or scurfy spot.
Roll : To wrap round on itself; to form into a spherical or cylindrical body by causing to turn over and over; as, to roll a sheet of paper; to roll parchment; to roll clay or putty into a ball.
Roll : To make a loud or heavy rumbling noise; as, the thunder rolls.
Roller : A cylinder coated with a composition made principally of glue and molassess, with which forms of type are inked previously to taking an impression from them.
Romaic : Of or relating to modern Greece, and especially to its language.
Romanesque : Somewhat resembling the Roman; -- applied sometimes to the debased style of the later Roman empire, but esp. to the more developed architecture prevailing from the 8th century to the 12th.
Romantic : Of or pertaining to the style of the Christian and popular literature of the Middle Ages, as opposed to the classical antique; of the nature of, or appropriate to, that style; as, the romantic school of poets.
Romeward : Tending or directed toward Rome, or toward the Roman Catholic Church.

Rota : A short-lived political club established in 1659 by J.Harrington to inculcate the democratic doctrine of election of the principal officers of the state by ballot, and the annual retirement of a portion of Parliament.
Rotator : A revolving reverberatory furnace.
Rother : A bovine beast.
Rotundity : Hence, completeness; entirety; roundness.
Rough : Not level; having a broken surface; uneven; -- said of a piece of land, or of a road.
Roughcast : To plaster with a mixture of lime and shells or pebbles; as, to roughcast a building.
Roughish : Somewhat rough.
Roulette : A game of chance, in which a small ball is made to move round rapidly on a circle divided off into numbered red and black spaces, the one on which it stops indicating the result of a variety of wagers permitted by the game.
Round : Full and smoothly expanded; not defective or abrupt; finished; polished; -- said of style, or of authors with reference to their style.
Round : Same as Round of beef, below.
Roundabout : Encircling; enveloping; comprehensive.
Rounder : An English game somewhat resembling baseball; also, another English game resembling the game of fives, but played with a football.
Roundness : Fullness; smoothness of flow; as, the roundness of a period; the roundness of a note; roundness of tone.
Rouse : To cause to start from a covert or lurking place; as, to rouse a deer or other animal of the chase.
Rout : A bellowing; a shouting; noise; clamor; uproar; disturbance; tumult.
Routinist : One who habituated to a routine.
Rover : A ball which has passed through all the hoops and would go out if it hit the stake but is continued in play; also, the player of such a ball.
Rowan : A european tree (Pyrus aucuparia) related to the apple, but with pinnate leaves and flat corymbs of small white flowers followed by little bright red berries. Called also roan tree, and mountain ash. The name is also applied to two American trees of similar habit (Pyrus Americana, and P. sambucifolia).
Rower : One who rows with an oar.
Royalization : The act of making loyal to a king.
Rubbing : of Rub
Rubber : One who, or that which, rubs.
Rubblework : Masonry constructed of unsquared stones that are irregular in size and shape.
Rubican : Colored a prevailing red, bay, or black, with flecks of white or gray especially on the flanks; -- said of horses.
Rubric : A titlepage, or part of it, especially that giving the date and place of printing; also, the initial letters, etc., when printed in red.
Ruby : Any species of South American humming birds of the genus Clytolaema. The males have a ruby-colored throat or breast.
Ruck : The common sort, whether persons or things; as, the ruck in a horse race.
Ruddle : A riddle or sieve.
Rudiment : An imperfect organ or part, or one which is never developed.
Rueful : Causing one to rue or lament; woeful; mournful; sorrowful.

Ruinable : Capable of being ruined.
Rule : An order regulating the practice of the courts, or an order made between parties to an action or a suit.
Ruler : A straight or curved strip of wood, metal, etc., with a smooth edge, used for guiding a pen or pencil in drawing lines. Cf. Rule, n., 7 (a).
Rumblingly : In a rumbling manner.

Rumor : A flying or popular report; the common talk; hence, public fame; notoriety.
Rumpless : Destitute of a rump.
Run : To proceed along a surface; to extend; to spread.
Run : To move rapidly by springing steps so that there is an instant in each step when neither foot touches the ground; -- so distinguished from walking in athletic competition.
Run : That which runs or flows in the course of a certain operation, or during a certain time; as, a run of must in wine making; the first run of sap in a maple orchard.
Runaway : The act of running away, esp. of a horse or teams; as, there was a runaway yesterday.
Rung : One of the rounds of a ladder.
Runner : A food fish (Elagatis pinnulatus) of Florida and the West Indies; -- called also skipjack, shoemaker, and yellowtail. The name alludes to its rapid successive leaps from the water.
Runt : Any animal which is unusually small, as compared with others of its kind; -- applied particularly to domestic animals.
Ruptured : of Rupture
Ruralize : To become rural; to go into the country; to rusticate.

-s : The suffix used to form the third person singular indicative of English verbs; as in falls, tells, sends.
Sabbath : Fig.: A time of rest or repose; intermission of pain, effort, sorrow, or the like.

Sacchariferous : Producing sugar; as, sacchariferous canes.
Saccharomyces : A genus of budding fungi, the various species of which have the power, to a greater or less extent, or splitting up sugar into alcohol and carbonic acid. They are the active agents in producing fermentation of wine, beer, etc. Saccharomyces cerevisiae is the yeast of sedimentary beer. Also called Torula.
Saccule : A little sac; specifically, the sacculus of the ear.
Sack : A bag for holding and carrying goods of any kind; a receptacle made of some kind of pliable material, as cloth, leather, and the like; a large pouch.

Safe : A place for keeping things in safety.

Salamstone : A kind of blue sapphire brought from Ceylon.
Salesmen : of Salesman
Salience : The quality or condition of being salient; a leaping; a springing forward; an assaulting.

Sambo : A colloquial or humorous appellation for a negro; sometimes, the offspring of a black person and a mulatto; a zambo.
Samoan : An inhabitant of the Samoan Islands.
Sanation : The act of healing or curing.
Sanctifyingly : In a manner or degree tending to sanctify or make holy.
Sanctuary : The most retired part of the temple at Jerusalem, called the Holy of Holies, in which was kept the ark of the covenant, and into which no person was permitted to enter except the high priest, and he only once a year, to intercede for the people; also, the most sacred part of the tabernacle; also, the temple at Jerusalem.
Sandal : A kind of shoe consisting of a sole strapped to the foot; a protection for the foot, covering its lower surface, but not its upper.
Sanders : An old name of sandalwood, now applied only to the red sandalwood. See under Sandalwood.

Sangreal : See Holy Grail, under Grail.
Sanguine : Blood color; red.
Sanhita : A collection of vedic hymns, songs, or verses, forming the first part of each Veda.
Sans : Without; deprived or destitute of. Rarely used as an English word.

Sassafras : An American tree of the Laurel family (Sassafras officinale); also, the bark of the roots, which has an aromatic smell and taste.
Sating : of Sate
Satinet : A kind of cloth made of cotton warp and woolen filling, used chiefly for trousers.
Satisfier : One who satisfies.
Saturant : Impregnating to the full; saturating.
Saturnalia : Hence: A period or occasion of general license, in which the passions or vices have riotous indulgence.
Sauba : A South American ant (Oecodoma cephalotes) remarkable for having two large kinds of workers besides the ordinary ones, and for the immense size of its formicaries. The sauba ant cuts off leaves of plants and carries them into its subterranean nests, and thus often does great damage by defoliating trees and cultivated plants.
Saucily : In a saucy manner; impudently; with impertinent boldness.
Saunders-blue : A kind of color prepared from calcined lapis lazuli; ultramarine; also, a blue prepared from carbonate of copper.
Saururae : An extinct order of birds having a long vertebrated tail with quills along each side of it. Archaeopteryx is the type. See Archaeopteryx, and Odontornithes.
Savage : Wild; untamed; uncultivated; as, savage beasts.
Save : Specifically, to deliver from sin and its penalty; to rescue from a state of condemnation and spiritual death, and bring into a state of spiritual life.
Saving : Avoiding unnecessary expense or waste; frugal; not lavish or wasteful; economical; as, a saving cook.
Savor : To partake of the quality or nature; to indicate the presence or influence; to smack; -- with of.
Sawed : of Saw
Sawfly : Any one of numerous species of hymenopterous insects belonging to the family Tenthredinidae. The female usually has an ovipositor containing a pair of sawlike organs with which she makes incisions in the leaves or stems of plants in which to lay the eggs. The larvae resemble those of Lepidoptera.
Saxicava : Any species of marine bivalve shells of the genus Saxicava. Some of the species are noted for their power of boring holes in limestone and similar rocks.
Saxonism : An idiom of the Saxon or Anglo-Saxon language.
Sayer : One who says; an utterer.
Scabbed : Abounding with scabs; diseased with scabs.
Scad : The cigar fish, or round robin.
Scalary : Resembling a ladder; formed with steps.

Scale : Relative dimensions, without difference in proportion of parts; size or degree of the parts or components in any complex thing, compared with other like things; especially, the relative proportion of the linear dimensions of the parts of a drawing, map, model, etc., to the dimensions of the corresponding parts of the object that is represented; as, a map on a scale of an inch to a mile.
Scale-winged : Having the wings covered with small scalelike structures, as the Lepidoptera; scaly-winged.

Scapegoat : A goat upon whose head were symbolically placed the sins of the people, after which he was suffered to escape into the wilderness.

Scarcity : The quality or condition of being scarce; smallness of quantity in proportion to the wants or demands; deficiency; lack of plenty; short supply; penury; as, a scarcity of grain; a great scarcity of beauties.

Schiller : The peculiar bronzelike luster observed in certain minerals, as hypersthene, schiller spar, etc. It is due to the presence of minute inclusions in parallel position, and is sometimes of secondary origin.
Schizo- : A combining form denoting division or cleavage; as, schizogenesis, reproduction by fission or cell division.

Scholastical : Scholastic.
School : The room or hall in English universities where the examinations for degrees and honors are held.

Schreibersite : A mineral occurring in steel-gray flexible folia. It contains iron, nickel, and phosphorus, and is found only in meteoric iron.

Sea : Any large holothurian, especially one of those belonging to the genus Pentacta, or Cucumaria, as the common American and European species. (P. frondosa).
Sea : A very large seal (Macrorhinus proboscideus) of the Antarctic seas, much hunted for its oil. It sometimes attains a length of thirty feet, and is remarkable for the prolongation of the nose of the adult male into an erectile elastic proboscis, about a foot in length. Another species of smaller size (M. angustirostris) occurs on the coast of Lower California, but is now nearly extinct.
Sea : A hydroid coral of the genus Millepora, especially M. alcicornis, of the West Indies and Florida. So called because it stings the tongue like ginger. See Illust. under Millepore.
Sea : A sea urchin.
Seal : An arrangement for preventing the entrance or return of gas or air into a pipe, by which the open end of the pipe dips beneath the surface of water or other liquid, or a deep bend or sag in the pipe is filled with the liquid; a draintrap.

Serve : To contribute or conduce to; to promote; to be sufficient for; to satisfy; as, to serve one's turn.
Service : A name given to several trees and shrubs of the genus Pyrus, as Pyrus domestica and P. torminalis of Europe, the various species of mountain ash or rowan tree, and the American shad bush (see Shad bush, under Shad). They have clusters of small, edible, applelike berries.

According to the English method, a million raised to the sixth power, or the number expressed by a unit with thirty-six ciphers annexed. See Numeration.

Short : Not prolonged, or relatively less prolonged, in utterance; -- opposed to long, and applied to vowels or to syllables. In English, the long and short of the same letter are not, in most cases, the long and short of the same sound; thus, the i in ill is the short sound, not of i in isle, but of ee in eel, and the e in pet is the short sound of a in pate, etc. See Quantity, and Guide to Pronunciation, //22, 30.

Skimmer : Any species of longwinged marine birds of the genus Rhynchops, allied to the terns, but having the lower mandible compressed and much longer than the upper one. These birds fly rapidly along the surface of the water, with the lower mandible immersed, thus skimming out small fishes. The American species (R. nigra) is common on the southern coasts of the United States. Called also scissorbill, and shearbill.

Sphere : In ancient astronomy, one of the concentric and eccentric revolving spherical transparent shells in which the stars, sun, planets, and moon were supposed to be set, and by which they were carried, in such a manner as to produce their apparent motions.

The rays are often long, but are sometimes so short as to appear only as angles to the disklike body. Called also sea star, five-finger, and stellerid.

Straight : Composed of cards which constitute a regular sequence, as the ace, king, queen, jack, and ten-spot; as, a straight hand; a straight flush.

Struthiones : In a wider sense, an extensive group of birds including the ostriches, cassowaries, emus, moas, and allied birds incapable of flight. In this sense it is equivalent to Ratitae, or Dromaeognathae.

Sulphindigotic : Of, pertaining to, or designating, a sulphonic acid obtained, as a blue solution, by dissolving indigo in sulphuric acid; -- formerly called also cerulic sulphuric acid, but properly called indigo-disulphonic acid.

Superposition : The act of superposing, or the state of being superposed; as, the superposition of rocks; the superposition of one plane figure on another, in geometry.

Swallow : Any one of numerous species of swifts which resemble the true swallows in form and habits, as the common American chimney swallow, or swift.

Sweat : Moisture issuing from any substance; as, the sweat of hay or grain in a mow or stack.

Sympathies : of Sympathy
Symphony : "An elaborate instrumental composition for a full orchestra, consisting usually, like the sonata, of three or four contrasted yet inwardly related movements, as the allegro, the adagio, the minuet and trio, or scherzo, and the finale in quick time. The term has recently been applied to large orchestral works in freer form, with arguments or programmes to explain their meaning, such as the ""symphonic poems"" of Liszt. The term was formerly applied to any composition for an orchestra, as overtures, etc., and still earlier, to certain compositions partly vocal, partly instrumental."
Symposiarch : The master of a feast.
Synagogue : The council of, probably, 120 members among the Jews, first appointed after the return from the Babylonish captivity; -- called also the Great Synagogue, and sometimes, though erroneously, the Sanhedrin.

Synchronization : The act of synchronizing; concurrence of events in respect to time.
Syncopating : of Syncopate
Syncytium : Tissue in which the cell or partition walls are wholly wanting and the cell bodies fused together, so that the tissue consists of a continuous mass of protoplasm in which nuclei are imbedded, as in ordinary striped muscle.
Syne : Late, -- as opposed to soon.
Syngenesia : A Linnaean class of plants in which the stamens are united by the anthers.

System : An assemblage of parts or organs, either in animal or plant, essential to the performance of some particular function or functions which as a rule are of greater complexity than those manifested by a single organ; as, the capillary system, the muscular system, the digestive system, etc.; hence, the whole body as a functional unity.

Tanghinia : The ordeal tree. See under Ordeal.

Tap : A tool for forming an internal screw, as in a nut, consisting of a hardened steel male screw grooved longitudinally so as to have cutting edges.

Tasseled : of Tassel
Taste : A particular sensation excited by the application of a substance to the tongue; the quality or savor of any substance as perceived by means of the tongue; flavor; as, the taste of an orange or an apple; a bitter taste; an acid taste; a sweet taste.
Tasty : Being in conformity to the principles of good taste; elegant; as, tasty furniture; a tasty dress.

Taxing : of Tax
Taxidermist : A person skilled in taxidermy.
Tea : To take or drink tea.
Teagle : A hoisting apparatus; an elevator; a crane; a lift.
Tear : A drop of the limpid, saline fluid secreted, normally in small amount, by the lachrymal gland, and diffused between the eye and the eyelids to moisten the parts and facilitate their motion. Ordinarily the secretion passes through the lachrymal duct into the nose, but when it is increased by emotion or other causes, it overflows the lids.
Tear-thumb : A name given to several species of plants of the genus Polygonum, having angular stems beset with minute reflexed prickles.
Teaseling : The cutting and gathering of teasels; the use of teasels.
Technic : The method of performance in any art; technical skill; artistic execution; technique.
Tectibranch : One of the Tectibranchiata. Also used adjectively.
Te : "An ancient and celebrated Christian hymn, of uncertain authorship, but often ascribed to St. Ambrose; -- so called from the first words ""Te Deum laudamus."" It forms part of the daily matins of the Roman Catholic breviary, and is sung on all occasions of thanksgiving. In its English form, commencing with words, ""We praise thee, O God,"" it forms a part of the regular morning service of the Church of England and the Protestant Episcopal Church in America."
Teem : To produce; to bring forth.
Teetered : of Teeter
Tegmen : The inner layer of the coating of a seed, usually thin and delicate; the endopleura.
Teinoscope : An instrument formed by combining prisms so as to correct the chromatic aberration of the light while linear dimensions of objects seen through the prisms are increased or diminished; -- called also prism telescope.
Telegraphy : The science or art of constructing, or of communicating by means of, telegraphs; as, submarine telegraphy.
Telephone : An instrument for reproducing sounds, especially articulate speech, at a distance.
Telescopy : The art or practice of using or making telescopes.
Tell : To give an account; to make report.
Tellural : Of or pertaining to the earth.
Telotrocha : An annelid larva having telotrochal bands of cilia.
Temper : To bring to a proper degree of hardness; as, to temper iron or steel.
Temperament : A system of compromises in the tuning of organs, pianofortes, and the like, whereby the tones generated with the vibrations of a ground tone are mutually modified and in part canceled, until their number reduced to the actual practicable scale of twelve tones to the octave. This scale, although in so far artificial, is yet closely suggestive of its origin in nature, and this system of tuning, although not mathematically true, yet satisfies the ear, while it has the convenience that the same twelve fixed tones answer for every key or scale, C/ becoming identical with D/, and so on.
Temperer : One who, or that which, tempers; specifically, a machine in which lime, cement, stone, etc., are mixed with water.
Temple : Hence, among Christians, an edifice erected as a place of public worship; a church.
Temporarily : In a temporary manner; for a time.
Tempting : of Tempt
Ten : One more than nine; twice five.
Tenacy : Tenaciousness; obstinacy.
Tend : To accompany as an assistant or protector; to care for the wants of; to look after; to watch; to guard; as, shepherds tend their flocks.
Tender : The thing offered; especially, money offered in payment of an obligation.
Tenderness : The quality or state of being tender (in any sense of the adjective).
Tenebrose : Characterized by darkness or gloom; tenebrous.
Tenne : A tincture, rarely employed, which is considered as an orange color or bright brown. It is represented by diagonal lines from sinister to dexter, crossed by vertical lines.
Ten-pounder : A large oceanic fish (Elops saurus) found in the tropical parts of all the oceans. It is used chiefly for bait.
Tensor : A muscle that stretches a part, or renders it tense.
Tentaculata : A division of Ctenophora including those which have two long tentacles.
Tentered : of Tenter
Tentiginous : Stiff; stretched; strained.
Tenuity : Refinement; delicacy.
Tephrosia : A genus of leguminous shrubby plants and herbs, mostly found in tropical countries, a few herbaceous species being North American. The foliage is often ashy-pubescent, whence the name.
Terbium : A rare metallic element, of uncertain identification, supposed to exist in certain minerals, as gadolinite and samarskite, with other rare ytterbium earth. Symbol Tr or Tb. Atomic weight 150.
Terebrae : of Terebra
Terete : Cylindrical and slightly tapering; columnar, as some stems of plants.
Term : The time for which anything lasts; any limited time; as, a term of five years; the term of life.
Termagant : An imaginary being supposed by the Christians to be a Mohammedan deity or false god. He is represented in the ancient moralities, farces, and puppet shows as extremely vociferous and tumultous.
Terminate : Hence, to put the finishing touch to; to bring to completion; to perfect.
Terminology : The doctrine of terms; a theory of terms or appellations; a treatise on terms.
Ternaries : of Ternary
Terracing : of Terrace

Terrific : Causing terror; adapted to excite great fear or dread; terrible; as, a terrific form; a terrific sight.
Territory : In the United States, a portion of the country not included within the limits of any State, and not yet admitted as a State into the Union, but organized with a separate legislature, under a Territorial governor and other officers appointed by the President and Senate of the United States. In Canada, a similarly organized portion of the country not yet formed into a Province.
Tertiary : Being of the third formation, order, or rank; third; as, a tertiary use of a word.
Tessellated : Marked like a checkerboard; as, a tessellated leaf.

Tetartohedral : Having one fourth the number of planes which are requisite to complete symmetry.
Tetra- : A combining form or prefix signifying four, as in tetrabasic, tetrapetalous.
Tetradactylous : Having, or characterized by, four digits to the foot or hand.
Tetragynia : A Linnaean order of plants having four styles.
Tetramorph : The union of the four attributes of the Evangelists in one figure, which is represented as winged, and standing on winged fiery wheels, the wings being covered with eyes. The representations of it are evidently suggested by the vision of Ezekiel (ch. i.)

Thalamocoele : The cavity or ventricle of the thalamencephalon; the third ventricle.
Thalline : An artificial alkaloid of the quinoline series, obtained as a white crystalline substance, C10H13NO, whose salts are valuable as antipyretics; -- so called from the green color produced in its solution by certain oxidizing agents.
Thane : A dignitary under the Anglo-Saxons and Danes in England. Of these there were two orders, the king's thanes, who attended the kings in their courts and held lands immediately of them, and the ordinary thanes, who were lords of manors and who had particular jurisdiction within their limits. After the Conquest, this title was disused, and baron took its place.
Thar : A goatlike animal (Capra Jemlaica) native of the Himalayas. It has small, flattened horns, curved directly backward. The hair of the neck, shoulders, and chest of the male is very long, reaching to the knees. Called also serow, and imo.
Thatching : The act or art of covering buildings with thatch; so as to keep out rain, snow, etc.
Thawy : Liquefying by heat after having been frozen; thawing; melting.
Theatin : Alt. of Theatine
Thecaphore : See Basigynium.

Theochristic : Anointed by God.

Thoracoplasty : A remodeling or reshaping of the thorax; especially, the operation of removing the ribs, so as to obliterate the pleural cavity in cases of empyema.
Thornbird : A small South American bird (Anumbius anumbii) allied to the ovenbirds of the genus Furnarius). It builds a very large and complex nest of twigs and thorns in a bush or tree.

Thou : The second personal pronoun, in the singular number, denoting the person addressed; thyself; the pronoun which is used in addressing persons in the solemn or poetical style.

Throttle : To breathe hard, as when nearly suffocated.
Thrown : of Throw
Throw : The extreme movement given to a sliding or vibrating reciprocating piece by a cam, crank, eccentric, or the like; travel; stroke; as, the throw of a slide valve. Also, frequently, the length of the radius of a crank, or the eccentricity of an eccentric; as, the throw of the crank of a steam engine is equal to half the stroke of the piston.
Thrum : To insert short pieces of rope-yarn or spun yarn in; as, to thrum a piece of canvas, or a mat, thus making a rough or tufted surface.
Thrust : To make a push; to attack with a pointed weapon; as, a fencer thrusts at his antagonist.
Thule : The name given by ancient geographers to the northernmost part of the habitable world. According to some, this land was Norway, according to others, Iceland, or more probably Mainland, the largest of the Shetland islands; hence, the Latin phrase ultima Thule, farthest Thule.
Thump : A blow or knock, as with something blunt or heavy; a heavy fall.
Thunderbolt : Vehement threatening or censure; especially, ecclesiastical denunciation; fulmination.
Thunderstruck : of Thunderstrike

Thymate : A compound of thymol analogous to a salt; as, sodium thymate.

Tibia : The fourth joint of the leg of an insect. See Illust. under Coleoptera, and under Hexapoda.

Tonic : "Of or relating to tones or sounds; specifically (Phon.), applied to, or distingshing, a speech sound made with tone unmixed and undimmed by obstruction, such sounds, namely, the vowels and diphthongs, being so called by Dr. James Rush (1833) "" from their forming the purest and most plastic material of intonation."""
Tonometer : An instrument for determining the rate of vibrations in tones.
Tonsured : Having the tonsure; shaven; shorn; clipped; hence, bald.

Tort : Any civil wrong or injury; a wrongful act (not involving a breach of contract) for which an action will lie; a form of action, in some parts of the United States, for a wrong or injury.
Tortrix : A genus of tropical short-tailed snakes, which are not venomous. One species (Tortrix scytalae) is handsomely banded with black, and is sometimes worn alive by the natives of Brazil for a necklace.
Torturous : Involving, or pertaining to, torture.
Tose : To tease, or comb, as wool.
Tossing : A process which consists in washing ores by violent agitation in water, in order to separate the lighter or earhy particles; -- called also tozing, and treloobing, in Cornwall.
Tote : To carry or bear; as, to tote a child over a stream; -- a colloquial word of the Southern States, and used esp. by negroes.
Tottery : Trembling or vaccilating, as if about to fall; unsteady; shaking.

Touching : Affecting; moving; pathetic; as, a touching tale.

Tourbillion : An ornamental firework which turns round, when in the air, so as to form a scroll of fire.

Trichinosis : The disease produced by the presence of trichinae in the muscles and intestinal track. It is marked by fever, muscular pains, and symptoms resembling those of typhoid fever, and is frequently fatal.

Turmeric : The root or rootstock of the Curcuma longa. It is externally grayish, but internally of a deep, lively yellow or saffron color, and has a slight aromatic smell, and a bitterish, slightly acrid taste. It is used for a dye, a medicine, a condiment, and a chemical test.
Turn : To move round; to have a circular motion; to revolve entirely, repeatedly, or partially; to change position, so as to face differently; to whirl or wheel round; as, a wheel turns on its axis; a spindle turns on a pivot; a man turns on his heel.

Un- : An inseparable prefix, or particle, signifying not; in-; non-. In- is prefixed mostly to words of Latin origin, or else to words formed by Latin suffixes; un- is of much wider application, and is attached at will to almost any adjective, or participle used adjectively, or adverb, from which it may be desired to form a corresponding negative adjective or adverb, and is also, but less freely, prefixed to nouns. Un- sometimes has merely an intensive force; as in unmerciless, unremorseless.

Ursuline : One of an order of nuns founded by St. Angela Merici, at Brescia, in Italy, about the year 1537, and so called from St. Ursula, under whose protection it was placed. Vaccine : any preparation used to render an organism immune to some disease, by inducing or increasing the natural immunity mechanisms. Prior to 1995, such preparations usually contained killed organisms of the type for which immunity was desired, and sometimes used live organisms having attenuated virulence. since that date, preparations containing only specific antigenic portions of the pathogenic organism are also used, some of which are prepared by genetic engineering techniques.

Vitriolated : Changed into a vitriol or a sulphate, or subjected to the action of sulphuric acid or of a sulphate; as, vitriolated potash, i. e., potassium sulphate.

Volow : To baptize; -- used in contempt by the Reformers.
Voltigeur : One of a picked company of irregular riflemen in each regiment of the French infantry.
Volumeter : An instrument for measuring the volumes of gases or liquids by introducing them into a vessel of known capacity.

Volutation : A rolling of a body; a wallowing.
Vomiting : of Vomit
Voodooism : A degraded form of superstition and sorcery, said to include human sacrifices and cannibalism in some of its rites. It is prevalent among the negroes of Hayti, and to some extent in the United States, and is regarded as a relic of African barbarism.
Votary : One devoted, consecrated, or engaged by a vow or promise; hence, especially, one devoted, given, or addicted, to some particular service, worship, study, or state of life.
Vouch : To call; to summon.
Vouchsafement : The act of vouchsafing, or that which is vouchsafed; a gift or grant in condescension.
Voyage : Course; way.
Vulcanist : A volcanist.
Vulgarized : of Vulgarize
Vulpic : Pertaining to, derived from, or designating, an acid obtained from a lichen (Cetraria vulpina) as a yellow or red crystalline substance which on decomposition yields pulvinic acid.
W : the twenty-third letter of the English alphabet, is usually a consonant, but sometimes it is a vowel, forming the second element of certain diphthongs, as in few, how. It takes its written form and its name from the repetition of a V, this being the original form of the Roman capital letter which we call U. Etymologically it is most related to v and u. See V, and U. Some of the uneducated classes in England, especially in London, confuse w and v, substituting the one for the other, as weal for veal, and veal for weal; wine for vine, and vine for wine, etc. See Guide to Pronunciation, // 266-268.
Wadding : Any soft stuff of loose texture, used for stuffing or padding garments; esp., sheets of carded cotton prepared for the purpose.
Wadsetter : One who holds by a wadset.
Waft : A wave or current of wind.
Wage : To expose one's self to, as a risk; to incur, as a danger; to venture; to hazard.
Waggel : The young of the great black-backed gull (Larus marinus), formerly considered a distinct species.
Wagonage : Money paid for carriage or conveyance in wagon.
Wail : To choose; to select.
Wainscot : Any one of numerous species of European moths of the family Leucanidae.
Waister : A seaman, usually a green hand or a broken-down man, stationed in the waist of a vessel of war.
Waive : A woman put out of the protection of the law. See Waive, v. t., 3 (b), and the Note.
Wake : To put in motion or action; to arouse; to excite.
Waking : A watch; a watching.
Walk : To move or go on the feet for exercise or amusement; to take one's exercise; to ramble.
Walker : Any ambulatorial orthopterous insect, as a stick insect.
Wallaroo : Any one of several species of kangaroos of the genus Macropus, especially M. robustus, sometimes called the great wallaroo.

Wallower : A lantern wheel; a trundle.
Wamble : Disturbance of the stomach; a feeling of nausea.
Wanderer : One who wanders; a rambler; one who roves; hence, one who deviates from duty.
Wanghee : The Chinese name of one or two species of bamboo, or jointed cane, of the genus Phyllostachys. The slender stems are much used for walking sticks.
Want : To feel need of; to wish or long for; to desire; to crave.
Wantonly : In a wanton manner; without regularity or restraint; loosely; sportively; gayly; playfully; recklessly; lasciviously.
Wappato : See Wapatoo.
Warble : A small, hard tumor which is produced on the back of a horse by the heat or pressure of the saddle in traveling.
Ward : One who, or that which, guards; garrison; defender; protector; means of guarding; defense; protection.
Wardcorps : Guardian; one set to watch over another.

Warehousing : The act of placing goods in a warehouse, or in a customhouse store.

Warm : To communicate a moderate degree of heat to; to render warm; to supply or furnish heat to; as, a stove warms an apartment.
Warning : of Warn

Wash-off : Capable of being washed off; not permanent or durable; -- said of colors not fixed by steaming or otherwise.
Wassailer : One who drinks wassail; one who engages in festivity, especially in drinking; a reveler.
Wasteboard : See Washboard, 3.
Wastrel : Anything cast away as bad or useless, as imperfect bricks, china, etc.
Watchet : Pale or light blue.
Watering : of Water
Water : A battery nearly on a level with the water.
Water : Any one of numerous species of large, rapacious, aquatic, hemipterous insects belonging to Belostoma, Benacus, Zaitha, and other genera of the family Belostomatidae. Their hind legs are long and fringed, and act like oars. Some of these insects are of great size, being among the largest existing Hemiptera. Many of them come out of the water and fly about at night.
Water : A color ground with water and gum or other glutinous medium; a color the vehicle of which is water; -- so called in distinction from oil color.
Water : See Water chevrotain.
Waterfall : A certain kind of neck scarf.
Water : An instrument for measuring or ascertaining the depth or quantity of water, or for indicating the height of its surface, as in the boiler of a steam engine. See Gauge.
Waterie : The pied wagtail; -- so called because it frequents ponds.
Water : A blossom or plant of any species of the genus Nymphaea, distinguished for its large floating leaves and beautiful flowers. See Nymphaea.
Water : A mill whose machinery is moved by water; -- distinguished from a windmill, and a steam mill.
Water : The ruddy duck.
Water : A pore by which the water tubes of various invertebrates open externally.
Water : The muskrat.
Watershed : The whole region or extent of country which contributes to the supply of a river or lake.
Water : Any spider that habitually lives on or about the water, especially the large American species (Dolomedes lanceolatus) which runs rapidly on the surface of water; -- called also raft spider.
Water : The common cat-tail (Typha latifolia), the spike of which makes a good torch soaked in oil.
Water : An American aquatic plant (Dianthera Americana) with long willowlike leaves, and spikes of small purplish flowers.
Wattle : The trees from which the bark is obtained. See Savanna wattle, under Savanna.

Wayz-goose : An annual feast of the persons employed in a printing office.
Weak : Lacking in elements of political strength; not wielding or having authority or energy; deficient in the resources that are essential to a ruler or nation; as, a weak monarch; a weak government or state.
Weak-minded : Having a weak mind, either naturally or by reason of disease; feebleminded; foolish; idiotic.
Wealthiness : The quality or state of being wealthy, or rich; richness; opulence.
Wear : To cause to go about, as a vessel, by putting the helm up, instead of alee as in tacking, so that the vessel's bow is turned away from, and her stern is presented to, the wind, and, as she turns still farther, her sails fill on the other side; to veer.
Weariless : Incapable of being wearied.
Weasel-faced : Having a thin, sharp face, like a weasel.
Weatherboard : That side of a vessel which is toward the wind; the windward side.
Weatherproof : Proof against rough weather.
Weazand : See Weasand.
Web : The membrane which unites the fingers or toes, either at their bases, as in man, or for a greater part of their length, as in many water birds and amphibians.
Webform : Any one of various species of moths whose gregarious larvae eat the leaves of trees, and construct a large web to which they retreat when not feeding.
Wedge : Anything in the form of a wedge, as a body of troops drawn up in such a form.
Wedlock : A wife; a married woman.
Weeder : One who, or that which, weeds, or frees from anything noxious.
Ween : To think; to imagine; to fancy.
Weeping : Pertaining to lamentation, or those who weep.

Weigh : To bear heavily; to press hard.
Weight : A definite mass of iron, lead, brass, or other metal, to be used for ascertaining the weight of other bodies; as, an ounce weight.

Welcomely : In a welcome manner.

Wend : p. p. of Wene.
Went : Course; way; path; journey; direction.
Weroole : An Australian lorikeet (Ptilosclera versicolor) noted for the variety of its colors; -- called also varied lorikeet.
West : To turn or move toward the west; to veer from the north or south toward the west.
Westy : Dizzy; giddy.
Wex : To grow; to wax.
Whahoo : An American tree, the winged elm. (Ulmus alata).

Wharf : To place upon a wharf; to bring to a wharf.
What : Why? For what purpose? On what account?
Wheatworm : A small nematode worm (Anguillula tritici) which attacks the grains of wheat in the ear. It is found in wheat affected with smut, each of the diseased grains containing a large number of the minute young of the worm.
Wheel : To convey on wheels, or in a wheeled vehicle; as, to wheel a load of hay or wood.
Wheeling : Condition of a road or roads, which admits of passing on wheels; as, it is good wheeling, or bad wheeling.
Whelk : A papule; a pustule; acne.
When : While; whereas; although; -- used in the manner of a conjunction to introduce a dependent adverbial sentence or clause, having a causal, conditional, or adversative relation to the principal proposition; as, he chose to turn highwayman when he might have continued an honest man; he removed the tree when it was the best in the grounds.
Whereabouts : Concerning which; about which.
Whereof : Of which; of whom; formerly, also, with which; -- used relatively.
Wherret : A box on the ear.
Whew : A sound like a half-formed whistle, expressing astonishment, scorn, or dislike.

Whinock : The small pig of a litter.

Whipperin : A huntsman who keeps the hounds from wandering, and whips them in, if necessary, to the of chase.
Whipworm : A nematode worm (Trichocephalus dispar) often found parasitic in the human intestine. Its body is thickened posteriorly, but is very long and threadlike anteriorly.
Whirlbone : The patella, or kneepan.
Whisk : A kind of cape, forming part of a woman's dress.
Whiskeys : of Whisky

White : Reflecting to the eye all the rays of the spectrum combined; not tinted with any of the proper colors or their mixtures; having the color of pure snow; snowy; -- the opposite of black or dark; as, white paper; a white skin.
Whitebelly : The American widgeon, or baldpate.
White-foot : A white mark on the foot of a horse, between the fetlock and the coffin.
Whitening : The act or process of making or becoming white.
Whitewashing : of Whitewash
Whiting : Any one of several species of North American marine sciaenoid food fishes belonging to genus Menticirrhus, especially M. Americanus, found from Maryland to Brazil, and M. littoralis, common from Virginia to Texas; -- called also silver whiting, and surf whiting.

Wholesale : Extensive and indiscriminate; as, wholesale slaughter.

Wicken : Same as Quicken tree.
Wide : Of large scope; comprehensive; liberal; broad; as, wide views; a wide understanding.

Widow-hunter : One who courts widows, seeking to marry one with a fortune.

Wigged : Having the head covered with a wig; wearing a wig.
Wild : Growing or produced without culture; growing or prepared without the aid and care of man; native; not cultivated; brought forth by unassisted nature or by animals not domesticated; as, wild parsnip, wild camomile, wild strawberry, wild honey.
Wilderness : Quality or state of being wild; wildness.
Wilk : See Whelk.

Wilt : Hence, to cause to languish; to depress or destroy the vigor and energy of.

Windmill : A mill operated by the power of the wind, usually by the action of the wind upon oblique vanes or sails which radiate from a horizontal shaft.
Windrowed : of Windrow
Wine : The effect of drinking wine in excess; intoxication.
Wing : Any membranaceous expansion, as that along the sides of certain stems, or of a fruit of the kind called samara.
Winged : Furnished with a leaflike appendage, as the fruit of the elm and the ash, or the stem in certain plants; alate.
Winking : of Wink
Winning : The act of obtaining something, as in a contest or by competition.
Winter : The season of the year in which the sun shines most obliquely upon any region; the coldest season of the year.
Winy : Having the taste or qualities of wine; vinous; as, grapes of a winy taste.
Wirche : To work
Wire-puller : One who pulls the wires, as of a puppet; hence, one who operates by secret means; an intriguer.
Wise : Way of being or acting; manner; mode; fashion.

Witch : One who practices the black art, or magic; one regarded as possessing supernatural or magical power by compact with an evil spirit, esp. with the Devil; a sorcerer or sorceress; -- now applied chiefly or only to women, but formerly used of men as well.

Withal : With; -- put after its object, at the end of sentence or clause in which it stands.

Withhold : To hold back; to restrain; to keep from action.
Withoutforth : Without; outside' outwardly. Cf. Withinforth.
Witness : One who is cognizant; a person who beholds, or otherwise has personal knowledge of, anything; as, an eyewitness; an earwitness.
Wittol : A man who knows his wife's infidelity and submits to it; a tame cuckold; -- so called because the cuckoo lays its eggs in the wittol's nest.

Wode : Mad. See Wood, a.
Wold : A plain, or low hill; a country without wood, whether hilly or not.
Wolframite : Tungstate of iron and manganese, generally of a brownish or grayish black color, submetallic luster, and high specific gravity. It occurs in cleavable masses, and also crystallized. Called also wolfram.

Wont : To be accustomed or habituated; to be used.

Woodman : One who cuts down trees; a woodcutter.

Wool : A sort of pubescence, or a clothing of dense, curling hairs on the surface of certain plants.

Work : Performance of moral duties; righteous conduct.

Workless : Not carried out in practice; not exemplified in fact; as, workless faith.
World : In a more restricted sense, that part of the earth and its concerns which is known to any one, or contemplated by any one; a division of the globe, or of its inhabitants; human affairs as seen from a certain position, or from a given point of view; also, state of existence; scene of life and action; as, the Old World; the New World; the religious world; the Catholic world; the upper world; the future world; the heathen world.
Worm : Same as Vermes.
Wormhole : A burrow made by a worm.
Worrisome : Inclined to worry or fret; also, causing worry or annoyance.

Yellow : A bright golden color, reflecting more light than any other except white; the color of that part of the spectrum which is between the orange and green.
Yellowness : The quality or state of being yellow; as, the yellowness of an orange.
Yellowwort : A European yellow-flowered, gentianaceous (Chlora perfoliata). The whole plant is intensely bitter, and is sometimes used as a tonic, and also in dyeing yellow.
Yeomanry : The position or rank of a yeoman.

Yet : Up to the present time; thus far; hitherto; until now; -- and with the negative, not yet, not up to the present time; not as soon as now; as, Is it time to go? Not yet. See As yet, under As, conj.

Yokelet : A small farm; -- so called as requiring but one yoke of oxen to till it.
York : The one of the three printed uses of England which was followed in the north. It was based on the Sarum use. See Use, n., 6.
Younker : A young person; a stripling; a yonker.

Ytterbium : A rare element of the boron group, sometimes associated with yttrium or other related elements, as in euxenite and gadolinite. Symbol Yb; provisional atomic weight 173.2. Cf. Yttrium.
Yulan : A species of Magnolia (M. conspicua) with large white blossoms that open before the leaves. See the Note under Magnolia.
Zaimet : A district from which a Zaim draws his revenue.
Zantiot : A native or inhabitant of Zante, one of the Ionian Islands.
Zea : A genus of large grasses of which the Indian corn (Zea Mays) is the only species known. Its origin is not yet ascertained. See Maize.
Zebrine : Pertaining to, or resembling, the zebra.
Zenith : That point in the visible celestial hemisphere which is vertical to the spectator; the point of the heavens directly overhead; -- opposed to nadir.
Zesting : of Zest
Zif : The second month of the Jewish ecclesiastical year, corresponding to our May.
Zincking : of Zinc
Zinco-polar : Electrically polarized like the surface of the zinc presented to the acid in a battery, which has zincous affinity.
Zircofluoride : A double fluoride of zirconium and hydrogen, or some other positive element or radical; as, zircofluoride of sodium.
Zoanthus : A genus of Actinaria, including numerous species, found mostly in tropical seas. The zooids or polyps resemble small, elongated actinias united together at their bases by fleshy stolons, and thus forming extensive groups. The tentacles are small and bright colored.
Zonae : of Zona
Zonule : A little zone, or girdle.
Zoogony : The doctrine of the formation of living beings.
Zoology : That part of biology which relates to the animal kingdom, including the structure, embryology, evolution, classification, habits, and distribution of all animals, both living and extinct.
Zoophily : Love of animals.
Zootic : Containing the remains of organized bodies; -- said of rock or soil.
Zoutch : To stew, as flounders, eels, etc., with just enough or liquid to cover them.
Zygobranchia : A division of marine gastropods in which the gills are developed on both sides of the body and the renal organs are also paired. The abalone (Haliotis) and the keyhole limpet (Fissurella) are examples.
Zylonite : Celluloid.
Zymotic : Of, pertaining to, or caused by, fermentation.
